Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Hierarchy of Zahir al-Riwayah Books
Explaining the chronology and authentication hierarchy of the six Zahir al-Riwayah books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the chronological order of the six Zahir al-Riwayah books and apply the rule that a later book takes precedence in fatwa.

Core Idea
In Zahir al-Riwayah, the later authored book supersedes the earlier, and 'al-Saghir' books carry Abu Yusuf's endorsement.

The Hanafi mufti must know which book of Zahir al-Riwayah to rely on when texts conflict. This lesson establishes the chronological order of Imam Muhammad's six core works and the authentication status of each, providing the first principle of textual tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six books in chronological order
List the six core books of Zahir al-Riwayah as given in the passage: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. Commit this order to memory.
al-Mabsut is first, al-Siyar al-Kabir is last.
2
Understand the rule: later book supersedes earlier
When two Zahir al-Riwayah books contradict, the later authored book is taken as authoritative, because the later author likely retracted or refined the earlier view. Example: al-Ziyadat (later) overrules al-Mabsut (earlier).
This is a settled principle in Hanafi mufti methodology.
3
Distinguish 'al-Saghir' from 'al-Kabir' books
Books with 'al-Saghir' in their title (e.g., al-Jami' al-Saghir) were reviewed and authenticated by Imam Abu Yusuf, adding weight. 'al-Kabir' books (e.g., al-Jami' al-Kabir) were not presented to Abu Yusuf, so they lack his endorsement.
This distinction affects reliability: al-Saghir books are more authoritative.
4
Recognize the special status of al-Jami' al-Saghir
Al-Jami' al-Saghir was authored by Imam Muhammad at Abu Yusuf's request and was the most relied upon by Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf carried it constantly and only objected to six masail in it.
This book is the most authenticated of the six, with only a handful of contested points.

Source Text

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي

وكل واحدٍ منهما ظاهرُ الرواية، عُمِل بالمتأخرة منهما زماناً. ربما يقع الاختلاف فيما بين كتب ظاهر الرواية، فحينئذ يؤخذ بالكتاب الذى تأخر تأليفه، فيصير خلافه كالمرجوع عنه، فلابد إذن من معرفة تاريخ هذه الكتب الستة. وقد ذكرنا فيما سبق أنّ أوّل هذه الكتب تأليفاً هو المبسوط، ثمّ الجامع الصغير ، ثمّ الجامع الكبير، ثم الزيادات، ثم السير الصغير، ثمّ السّير الكبير. فإن وقع التعارض مثلاً فيما بين المبسوط والزيادات ، يُختار ما في الزيادات، لكونه متأخراً. و ينبغي أن يُعلم أن الكتب التى يوجد فى آخر أسمائها لفظ "الصغير" كلها موثقة من قبل الإمام أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أيضاً. وأما ما جاء فيه لفظ "الكبير" فلم يعرضها الإمام محمّد على الإمام أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى، فليس موثقاً من قبله، كالجامع الكبير والسير الكبير والمزارعة الكبير والمأذون الكبير. وكان من أكثر كتب الامام محمد اعتمادا من قبل الإمام أبي يوسف رحمهما الله تعالى هو "الجامع الصغير". فإنّه ألفه الإمام محمد بأمر الإمام أبي يوسف، وقد ذكرنا في تعريف هذا الكتاب أن أبا يوسف رحمه الله تعالى كان يصحب هذا الكتاب في سفره و حضره، ولم ينكر منه شيئا إلا ست مسائل خطأ فيها الإمام محمدا في رواية قول أبي حنيفة، وقد ذكر هذه المسائل الستة ابن نجيم في باب الوتر والنوافل من البحر الرائق. فاختلف المشايخ الحنفية في الترجيح بين القولين فى هذه المسائل الستة. فقال بعض المشايخ يرجح قول محمد علي قول أبي يوسف، وخالفهم آخرون فرجحوا قول أبي يوسف. ودليل المشايخ الذين يرجحون قول أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى أن محمدا إنما روى هذه الأقوال عن أبي يوسف، فلما أنكر أبو يوسف

بطلت روايته. ولكن أكثر المشايخ على ترجيح قول محمد، وذلك لوجوه الوجه الأول: أنه قد تقرر في أصول الحديث أن نسيان المروي عنه روايته لا يُبطل الرواية إذا كان الراوى عنه ثقة.
ولكن جريان هذا الأصل في المسألة المبحوث عنها مشكل، لأن ذلك الأصل فيما إذا نسي المروي عنه. أما إذا صرّح المروي عنه بأنه رواه بخلاف ما روى عنه تلميذه، وجزم بذلك، فلا يتأتى هذا الأصل والأمر في هذه المسائل السنّة أن أبا يوسف رحمه الله تعالى لم يعترف بنسيانه، وإنما جزم بروايةٍ تُخالف رواية محمد رحمه الله تعالى.
الوجه الثاني: أن الإمام محمداً رحمه الله تعالى قد أنكر على أبي يوسف :وقال: "حفظتها ونسي " وجزمه هذا يدل علي أنه سمع هذه المسائل عن أبى حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى بلا واسطةٍ أيضاً، فلو بطلت روايته بواسطة الإمام أبي
يوسف، ثبتت روايته عن أبى حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى بلا واسطة. الوجه الثالث: أنه يمكن أن يكون محمد خرج هذه المسائل علي أصل أبى
حنيفة رحمهما الله تعالى، وحينئذ لا يؤثر إنكار أبي يوسف عليه. الوجه الرابع أن المشايخ ذكروا أن رواية محمد استحسان ورواية أبى
يوسف رحمه الله تعالى قياس والاستحسان راجح على القياس. وبالرغم ممّا ذُكر من أنه حيث لم يوجد ترجيح من أصحاب الترجيح يؤخذ بظاهر الرواية، فقد ذكر ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في منظومة "رسم المفتى " ضوابط أخرى يُستأنس بها عند الإفتاء، وهي: ۱ - يؤخذ بقول الإمام أبي حنيفة فى العبادات مطلقاً. ٢- يؤخذ بقول الإمام أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء.
Summary of the rules of Rasm al-Mufti. Each of them is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the later one in time is acted upon. Sometimes difference occurs between the books of Zahir al-Riwayah; then the book that was authored later is taken, so its opposition becomes like a retraction. Therefore, the history of these six books must be known. We have mentioned earlier that the first of these books authored is al-Mabsut, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat, then al-Siyar al-Saghir, then al-Siyar al-Kabir. If a conflict occurs, e.g., between al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat, what is in al-Ziyadat is chosen because it is later. It should be known that the books in whose names the word "al-Saghir" appears are all also authenticated by Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him. As for those with the word "al-Kabir", Imam Muhammad did not present them to Imam Abu Yusuf, so they are not authenticated by him, such as al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Muzara'ah al-Kabir, and al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir. The most relied upon of Imam Muhammad's books by Imam Abu Yusuf was "al-Jami' al-Saghir". Indeed, Imam Muhammad authored it by the order of Imam Abu Yusuf, and we have mentioned in the definition of this book that Abu Yusuf used to carry this book in his travel and residence, and he did not criticize anything in it except six masail in which he corrected Imam Muhammad regarding the transmission of Abu Hanifa's statement. These six masail were mentioned by Ibn Nujaym in the chapter of Witr and Nawafil from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The Hanafi scholars differed regarding the preference between the two opinions in these six masail. Some scholars said the statement of Muhammad is given preference over the statement of Abu Yusuf, while others disagreed and gave preference to Abu Yusuf's statement. The evidence of those who prefer the statement of Abu Yusuf is that Muhammad only transmitted these statements from Abu Yusuf, so when Abu Yusuf rejected it, his transmission became invalid. But most scholars are of the view that Muhammad's statement is preferred, due to the following reasons: First: It is established in usul al-hadith that the forgetfulness of the person from whom it is transmitted does not invalidate the transmission if the transmitter is reliable. However, applying this principle to the matter under discussion is problematic, because the principle applies when the person from whom it is transmitted forgets. But if the person from whom it is transmitted explicitly states that he transmitted it contrary to what his student transmitted from him, and is definite about it, this principle does not apply. In these six masail, Abu Yusuf did not admit to forgetfulness; rather, he was definite about a narration contradictory to Muhammad's narration. Second: Imam Muhammad objected to Abu Yusuf and said: "I preserved it and he forgot." This certainty of his indicates that he heard these masail directly from Abu Hanifa as well. So even if his transmission through Abu Yusuf is invalidated, his transmission directly from Abu Hanifa remains valid. Third: It is possible that Muhammad derived these masail based on Abu Hanifa's principles, and in that case Abu Yusuf's objection does not affect it. Fourth: The scholars mentioned that Muhammad's narration is istihsan, and Abu Yusuf's narration is qiyas, and istihsan is given precedence over qiyas. Despite what has been mentioned that when there is no preference from the authorities, the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) is taken, Ibn 'Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in his poem "Rasm al-Mufti" other guidelines that may be used for fatwa: 1) The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is taken absolutely in acts of worship. 2) The statement of Imam Abu Yusuf is taken in matters pertaining to judiciary.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed methodology for the Hanafi mufti when faced with conflicting transmissions within the school. The author begins by summarizing a key rule: when two books from Zahir al-Riwayah conflict, the later one in composition is preferred, as the later author likely revised or retracted the earlier view. Hence, knowing the chronology of the six major books of Imam Muhammad is essential. The author lists them in order: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. A further refinement is that books with 'al-Saghir' in their titles were reviewed and authenticated by Imam Abu Yusuf, giving them additional authority. The most relied upon of Muhammad's books by Abu Yusuf was al-Jami' al-Saghir, which Abu Yusuf carried with him constantly, and he only disputed six masail where he claimed Muhammad misstated Abu Hanifa's position. This led to a disagreement among later Hanafi scholars on how to prefer between the two imams in these six masail. The passage gives the arguments of both sides: those preferring Abu Yusuf argue that Muhammad's transmission was based on what he heard from Abu Yusuf, so when Abu Yusuf denied it, the transmission falls. The majority, however, prefer Muhammad's view for four reasons: (1) The principle that a narrator's forgetfulness does not invalidate a reliable transmission, but this is problematic here because Abu Yusuf did not claim forgetfulness but was certain. (2) Muhammad claimed direct hearing from Abu Hanifa, so even if one chain is broken, another remains. (3) Muhammad may have derived the rulings from Abu Hanifa's general principles, independent of specific narrations. (4) Muhammad's view is istihsan (juristic preference) while Abu Yusuf's is qiyas (analogy), and istihsan is stronger. Finally, the passage notes that despite these specific rules, Ibn 'Abidin in his Rasm al-Mufti gives broader heuristics: in acts of worship (ibadat), always follow Abu Hanifa's opinion; in judiciary matters (qada), follow Abu Yusuf; and presumably other categories for Muhammad or the later scholars. This passage equips the mufti with both the detailed hierarchy of texts and the general principles of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad that contain the authoritative narrations of the Hanafi school
رسم المفتي (Rasm al-Mufti): The protocol or methodology for a Hanafi mufti to issue fatwas, including rules for preferring texts and opinions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a conflict arises between al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat, which book's ruling should be given precedence?
A) Al-Mabsut
B) Al-Ziyadat
C) Neither, the mufti must seek a third source
D) It depends on the subject matter

Key Takeaway
The chronological order of Zahir al-Riwayah books determines which ruling takes precedence: later books supersede earlier ones, and al-Saghir books have additional authentication from Abu Yusuf.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
Preferring Between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf in Contested Narrations
Analysing the intra-Hanafi dispute over six masail and the tarjih mechanism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six masail of disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, state the arguments of both sides, and apply the preferred view (tarjih) in fatwa.

Core Idea
In the six masail, the majority prefers Imam Muhammad's narration, supported by direct hearing from Abu Hanifa and the strength of istihsan over qiyas.

Even the most authoritative of Imam Muhammad's books, al-Jami' al-Saghir, contains six masail where Abu Yusuf disputed the transmission. This lesson analyses the scholarly debate on which imam's view takes precedence and provides the mufti with the operative ruling for these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six masail and the nature of the disagreement
These are six specific rulings in al-Jami' al-Saghir where Abu Yusuf claimed that Imam Muhammad incorrectly transmitted Abu Hanifa's position. Abu Yusuf asserted his own version as correct.
The masail are not enumerated in this passage, but referenced from Ibn Nujaym's al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
2
Understand the opposing evidence for preferring Abu Yusuf
The minority view: Muhammad transmitted these from Abu Yusuf; when Abu Yusuf denied the transmission, the chain is broken, so Muhammad's narration becomes invalid.
This argument relies on the chain of transmission (silsila).
3
Analyse the four reasons supporting the majority preference for Muhammad
The majority gives four reasons: (1) The principle that a narrator's forgetfulness does not invalidate a reliable transmission, though here Abu Yusuf claimed certainty, not forgetfulness; (2) Muhammad claimed direct hearing from Abu Hanifa, so even if the through-Abu-Yusuf chain fails, another remains; (3) Muhammad may have derived the rulings from Abu Hanifa's general principles; (4) Muhammad's view is istihsan, which is stronger than qiyas (Abu Yusuf's view).
Reason (4) is considered the strongest: istihsan overrules qiyas in Hanafi methodology.
4
Recognize the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The majority of Hanafi scholars prefer Muhammad's narration in these six masail. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
Despite the disagreement, the later authoritativeness of al-Jami' al-Saghir and the reasoning in favor of Muhammad tip the scales.
5
Note Ibn 'Abidin's additional guidelines for fatwa
Ibn 'Abidin in Rasm al-Mufti provides two broad heuristics: (1) In acts of worship (ibadat), always follow Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion. (2) In judiciary matters (qada), follow Imam Abu Yusuf's opinion. These serve as general rules when no specific tarjih exists.
These guidelines help a mufti navigate other disagreements beyond the six masail.

Source Text

تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي

Summary of the rules of Rasm al-Mufti. Each of them is from Zahir al-Riwayah; the later one in time is acted upon. Sometimes difference occurs between the books of Zahir al-Riwayah; then the book that was authored later is taken, so its opposition becomes like a retraction. Therefore, the history of these six books must be known. We have mentioned earlier that the first of these books authored is al-Mabsut, then al-Jami' al-Saghir, then al-Jami' al-Kabir, then al-Ziyadat, then al-Siyar al-Saghir, then al-Siyar al-Kabir. If a conflict occurs, e.g., between al-Mabsut and al-Ziyadat, what is in al-Ziyadat is chosen because it is later. It should be known that the books in whose names the word "al-Saghir" appears are all also authenticated by Imam Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him. As for those with the word "al-Kabir", Imam Muhammad did not present them to Imam Abu Yusuf, so they are not authenticated by him, such as al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Muzara'ah al-Kabir, and al-Ma'dhun al-Kabir. The most relied upon of Imam Muhammad's books by Imam Abu Yusuf was "al-Jami' al-Saghir". Indeed, Imam Muhammad authored it by the order of Imam Abu Yusuf, and we have mentioned in the definition of this book that Abu Yusuf used to carry this book in his travel and residence, and he did not criticize anything in it except six masail in which he corrected Imam Muhammad regarding the transmission of Abu Hanifa's statement. These six masail were mentioned by Ibn Nujaym in the chapter of Witr and Nawafil from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The Hanafi scholars differed regarding the preference between the two opinions in these six masail. Some scholars said the statement of Muhammad is given preference over the statement of Abu Yusuf, while others disagreed and gave preference to Abu Yusuf's statement. The evidence of those who prefer the statement of Abu Yusuf is that Muhammad only transmitted these statements from Abu Yusuf, so when Abu Yusuf rejected it, his transmission became invalid. But most scholars are of the view that Muhammad's statement is preferred, due to the following reasons: First: It is established in usul al-hadith that the forgetfulness of the person from whom it is transmitted does not invalidate the transmission if the transmitter is reliable. However, applying this principle to the matter under discussion is problematic, because the principle applies when the person from whom it is transmitted forgets. But if the person from whom it is transmitted explicitly states that he transmitted it contrary to what his student transmitted from him, and is definite about it, this principle does not apply. In these six masail, Abu Yusuf did not admit to forgetfulness; rather, he was definite about a narration contradictory to Muhammad's narration. Second: Imam Muhammad objected to Abu Yusuf and said: "I preserved it and he forgot." This certainty of his indicates that he heard these masail directly from Abu Hanifa as well. So even if his transmission through Abu Yusuf is invalidated, his transmission directly from Abu Hanifa remains valid. Third: It is possible that Muhammad derived these masail based on Abu Hanifa's principles, and in that case Abu Yusuf's objection does not affect it. Fourth: The scholars mentioned that Muhammad's narration is istihsan, and Abu Yusuf's narration is qiyas, and istihsan is given precedence over qiyas. Despite what has been mentioned that when there is no preference from the authorities, the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah) is taken, Ibn 'Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned in his poem "Rasm al-Mufti" other guidelines that may be used for fatwa: 1) The statement of Imam Abu Hanifa is taken absolutely in acts of worship. 2) The statement of Imam Abu Yusuf is taken in matters pertaining to judiciary.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed methodology for the Hanafi mufti when faced with conflicting transmissions within the school. The author begins by summarizing a key rule: when two books from Zahir al-Riwayah conflict, the later one in composition is preferred, as the later author likely revised or retracted the earlier view. Hence, knowing the chronology of the six major books of Imam Muhammad is essential. The author lists them in order: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. A further refinement is that books with 'al-Saghir' in their titles were reviewed and authenticated by Imam Abu Yusuf, giving them additional authority. The most relied upon of Muhammad's books by Abu Yusuf was al-Jami' al-Saghir, which Abu Yusuf carried with him constantly, and he only disputed six masail where he claimed Muhammad misstated Abu Hanifa's position. This led to a disagreement among later Hanafi scholars on how to prefer between the two imams in these six masail. The passage gives the arguments of both sides: those preferring Abu Yusuf argue that Muhammad's transmission was based on what he heard from Abu Yusuf, so when Abu Yusuf denied it, the transmission falls. The majority, however, prefer Muhammad's view for four reasons: (1) The principle that a narrator's forgetfulness does not invalidate a reliable transmission, but this is problematic here because Abu Yusuf did not claim forgetfulness but was certain. (2) Muhammad claimed direct hearing from Abu Hanifa, so even if one chain is broken, another remains. (3) Muhammad may have derived the rulings from Abu Hanifa's general principles, independent of specific narrations. (4) Muhammad's view is istihsan (juristic preference) while Abu Yusuf's is qiyas (analogy), and istihsan is stronger. Finally, the passage notes that despite these specific rules, Ibn 'Abidin in his Rasm al-Mufti gives broader heuristics: in acts of worship (ibadat), always follow Abu Hanifa's opinion; in judiciary matters (qada), follow Abu Yusuf; and presumably other categories for Muhammad or the later scholars. This passage equips the mufti with both the detailed hierarchy of texts and the general principles of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad that contain the authoritative narrations of the Hanafi school
استحسان (istihsan): A method of juristic preference based on equity or custom, considered stronger than qiyas (analogy) in the Hanafi school
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from a primary source to a new case

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the six masail where Abu Yusuf disputed Imam Muhammad, which of the following is NOT a reason given by the majority to prefer Muhammad's narration?
A) Muhammad preserved the correct narration and Abu Yusuf forgot
B) Muhammad heard directly from Abu Hanifa
C) Muhammad's view is based on qiyas, which is stronger
D) Istihsan overrides qiyas

Key Takeaway
In the six masail, the majority of Hanafi scholars prefer Imam Muhammad's narration, supported by direct hearing from Abu Hanifa and the principle that istihsan overrides qiyas.

Six Guidelines for the Mufti from Rasm al-Mufti
Six rules for mufti preference and hierarchy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six rules for selecting opinions from Rasm al-Mufti and apply them to hypothetical fatwa scenarios.

Core Idea
Fatwa is not free choice: strict rules from Rasm al-Mufti govern which imam's opinion to follow in worship, judiciary, and inheritance, and which texts to prioritize.

When a mufti faces multiple opinions and no explicit tarjih from the scholars, he is not free to pick any. Ibn Abidin's 'Rasm al-Mufti' provides six concrete guidelines that direct him to specific imams for specific fields and establish a clear hierarchy of textual sources. These rules ensure consistency and discipline in Hanafi fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default starting point
Recognize that in the absence of a specific tarjih, the default is to follow zahir al-riwayah—the well-known transmitted opinions from the early Hanafi imams.
This is the baseline before applying the six special rules.
2
List the three imams and their specialized areas
Memorize that Abu Hanifa's opinion is absolute in worship, Abu Yusuf's is followed in judiciary, and Muhammad's in inheritance of distant relatives.
These are not arbitrary; each imam had particular expertise or practice.
3
Understand the principle of dirayah with riwayah
If a ruling is supported by both transmitted text (riwayah) and rational understanding (dirayah), do not abandon it for a mere text without understanding.
This ensures that the mufti uses both transmission and intellect.
4
Apply the caution regarding declaring kufr
Never issue a fatwa of kufr if there is any possible good interpretation or any disagreement among scholars, even if based on a weak report.
This reflects the Hanafi principle of leniency in matters of faith.
5
Apply the hierarchy of texts
Prioritize reliable matn works (primary texts) over commentaries, and commentaries over fatwa collections. Recognize the list of reliable matn works and note that some later works are actually fatwa collections.
This prevents relying on secondary sources when primary texts are available.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالرغم ممّا ذُكر من أنه حيث لم يوجد ترجيح من أصحاب الترجيح يؤخذ بظاهر الرواية، فقد ذكر ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في منظومة "رسم المفتى " ضوابط أخرى يُستأنس بها عند الإفتاء، وهي: ۱ - يؤخذ بقول الإمام أبي حنيفة فى العبادات مطلقاً. ٢- يؤخذ بقول الإمام أبي يوسف فيما يتعلق بالقضاء. ٣- يؤخذ بقول الإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيما يتعلق بتوريث ذوي الأرحام. ٤- لا يُعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية. ه - لا يفتي بكفر مسلم أمكن حمل كلامه على مَحْمِلٍ حسن، أوكان فى كُفره اختلاف، ولو رواية ضعيفة. ٦ - يقدم مافى المتون المعتبرة على الشروح ، ومافي الشروح على الفتاوى. والمتون المعتبرة مختصر القدوري، والمختار، والثقاية، والوقاية، والكنز، والمنتقى، بخلاف متن "الغرر " لملاً خُسرو ، ومتن "التنوير" للتُمُرْتَاشِي الغَزّي ، فإن فيهما كثيراً من مسائل الفتاوى.
Despite what was mentioned, that where there is no preference from the scholars of tarjih, one acts upon the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in his poem 'Rasm al-Mufti' other guidelines to be used for fatwa: 1. The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa is taken in acts of worship absolutely. 2. The opinion of Imam Abu Yusuf is taken regarding judiciary matters. 3. The opinion of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) is taken regarding inheritance of distant relatives (dhawi al-arham). 4. One does not depart from direct transmission (dirayah) when it agrees with narration (riwayah). 5. One does not issue a fatwa of kufr against a Muslim if it is possible to interpret his words in a good way, or if there is disagreement about his kufr, even if a weak narration. 6. What is in the reliable matn works is given precedence over commentaries, and what is in commentaries over fatwa collections. And the reliable matn works are: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Thiqayah? (al-Wiqayah), al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, al-Muntaqa, unlike the matn 'al-Ghurar' by Mulla Khusraw and the matn 'al-Tanwir' by al-Tumurtashi al-Ghazzi, for they contain many issues of fatwas (not purely matn).
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage summarizes key rules for the mufti from Ibn Abidin's poetic work 'Rasm al-Mufti'. It begins by stating that in the absence of a specific tarjih from the scholars, the default is to follow zahir al-riwayah (the well-known transmitted opinions from the founding imams). Then it provides six specific guidelines: (1) In worship (ibadat), the ruling of Abu Hanifa is followed unconditionally, because worship is based on strict transmission. (2) In judiciary (qada), the opinion of Abu Yusuf is given weight, presumably because he served as chief judge and was more experienced in court matters. (3) For inheritance of dhawi al-arham (distant relatives who are not Quranic heirs or agnates), Imam Muhammad's rulings are followed, as he specialized in this area. (4) Do not abandon a ruling that is supported by both textual transmission (riwayah) and rational understanding (dirayah); i.e., prefer it over mere text without understanding. (5) Be extremely cautious in declaring a Muslim a kafir; if there is any possible good interpretation, or any disagreement among scholars about his kufr, even if based on a weak report, do not issue a fatwa of kufr. (6) The hierarchy of sources: first consult the reliable matn works (primary texts), then commentaries (shuruh), then fatwa collections. The passage lists the recognized matn works and notes that some later works like al-Ghurar and al-Tanwir are actually collections of fatwas rather than pure matn, so they belong to a lower rank. This illustrates the Hanafi methodology of preferring foundational texts over later interpretations.

Key Terms
الدراية (dirayah): Understanding or comprehension of the law; the jurist's reasoning that aligns with transmitted narration.
المتون المعتبرة (al-mutun al-mu'tabara): The reliable primary textual works of the Hanafi school, such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, etc.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-established and apparent transmitted opinions from the early Hanafi imams, especially from the six books of Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Abu Hanifa
B) Abu Yusuf
C) Muhammad
D) The opinion of the majority of later scholars

Key Takeaway
A mufti must apply the six rules of Rasm al-Mufti to determine which imam's opinion to follow and which text to prioritize, ensuring methodological consistency in fatwa.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Rules for the Mufti: Preference and Limitations
Methodological summary for muftis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the hierarchical rules for source selection in Hanafi fatwa and apply the principle of avoiding takfir when any good interpretation is possible.

Core Idea
A mufti must prioritize reliable texts, preserve Muslimhood, and ultimately rely on juristic intuition developed through practice.

The passage presents key rules from Rasm al-Mufti, guiding the mufti in selecting authoritative opinions and avoiding dangerous errors like takfir. These rules are not mechanical but require deep juristic insight. This lesson will help you internalize these principles as foundational tools for fatwa practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five explicit rules
Read the passage and list each rule: (1) follow Imam Muhammad for Dhawil Arham, (2) do not abandon dirayah when riwayah agrees, (3) avoid takfir if any good interpretation exists, (4) hierarchy: mutun > shuruh > fatwas, (5) rules are not universal; rely on malakah.
Rule 3 is particularly important for preserving the status of Muslims.
2
Understand the hierarchy of sources
Note which texts are considered reliable mutun (al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, etc.) and why they take precedence over commentaries and later fatwas. Recognize the exception of al-Ghurar and al-Tanwir.
The hierarchy is a tool, not an absolute; the mufti's judgment is final.
3
Apply the takfir rule
Practice the principle: if a Muslim's statement can be interpreted favorably, do not declare kufr. Even if a weak transmission suggests kufr, the inclination is towards preserving iman.
This reflects the Hanafi maxim 'al-ghalib la yu'bar' and prioritizes mercy.
4
Recognize the role of malakah fiqhiyyah
Understand that the rules are 'istinas' (aids). The ultimate reference is the juristic intuition developed through long practice and companionship with scholars.
This prevents the mufti from applying rules mechanically without deeper understanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يؤخذ بقول الإمام محمد رحمه الله تعالى فيما يتعلق بتوريث ذوي الأرحام. ٤- لا يُعدل عن الدراية إذا وافقتها رواية.
ه - لا يفتي بكفر مسلم أمكن حمل كلامه على مَحْمِلٍ حسن، أوكان فى كُفره اختلاف، ولو رواية ضعيفة.
٦ - يقدم مافى المتون المعتبرة على الشروح ، ومافي الشروح على الفتاوى. والمتون المعتبرة مختصر القدوري، والمختار، والثقاية، والوقاية، والكنز، والمنتقى، بخلاف متن "الغرر" لملاً خُسرو ، ومتن "التنوير" للتُمُرْتَاشِي الغَزّي ، فإن فيهما كثيراً من مسائل الفتاوى.
ولكن هذه الضوابط ليست كلية مطردة في جميع الأحوال، كما لا يخفى على من سبر المسائل، وإنما ذكرت للاستئناس بها، وإلا فالمرجع في مثل ذلك، كما قدمنا في الأصل الثّامن إلى الملكة الفقهية والمذاق الصحيح الذى لا يحصل إلا بالممارسة الطويلة وصحبة المتمكنين من الفقهاء والمفتين.
One follows the statement of Imam Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on him) concerning inheritance by Dhawil Arham. 4- One does not depart from [what is established by] knowledge when a narration agrees with it. 5- One does not declare a Muslim an unbeliever if his words can be interpreted in a good way, or if there is disagreement about his disbelief, even if through a weak narration. 6- What is in the reliable texts is given precedence over commentaries, and what is in commentaries over fatwas. The reliable texts are: Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Mukhtar, al-Thiqayah, al-Wiqayah, al-Kanz, al-Muntaqa—unlike the text 'al-Ghurar' by Mulla Khusraw and the text 'al-Tanwir' by al-Tumurtashi al-Ghazzi, for both contain many issues from fatwas. But these guidelines are not universal and consistent in all cases, as is not hidden from one who has surveyed the issues. They are mentioned only for assistance; otherwise, the reference in such matters, as we have presented in the eighth principle, is to fiqh intuition and correct taste, which is only attained through long practice and companionship with accomplished jurists and muftis.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage presents a set of methodological rules for the mufti, drawn from the summary of Rasm al-Mufti. The first rule instructs the mufti to follow the transmission of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani specifically in matters of inheritance for Dhawil Arham (distant kindred). This reflects the Hanafi school's reliance on Imam Muhammad's works (Zahir al-Riwayah) in this area. The second rule (number 4) emphasizes that the mufti should not abandon what is established by reliable knowledge (dirayah) when it is supported by a transmitted narration (riwayah). The third rule (number 5) is a critical caution against takfir: the mufti must avoid declaring a Muslim an unbeliever if there is any possible good interpretation of his words, or if there is any disagreement (khilaf) regarding the issue, even if the dissenting opinion is weak. This underscores the Hanafi principle of minimizing takfir. The fourth rule (number 6) establishes a hierarchy of sources: the sound mutun (abridged texts) take precedence over commentaries (shuruh), and commentaries over later fatwa collections. The listed mutun are the core Hanafi works. However, the text warns that these guidelines are not universally applicable; they are merely aids. The ultimate reference, as stated in the earlier eighth principle, is the juristic faculty (malakah fiqhiyyah) and correct legal taste (dhawq), which are developed only through extensive study and association with proficient scholars. This reflects the Hanafi view that fiqh is not purely mechanical; the mufti must develop deep understanding.

Key Terms
ذوي الأرحام (Dhawil Arham): Distant kindred, relatives who are neither ashab al-faraid nor asabah.
الدراية (al-dirayah): Knowledge derived from reasoning and understanding, as opposed to narration (riwayah).
المتون المعتبرة (al-mutun al-mu'tabarah): The reliable abridged texts of Hanafi fiqh that are considered authoritative sources for fatwa.
الملكة الفقهية (al-malakah al-fiqhiyyah): The inner juristic faculty or intuition acquired through long practice and study.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Commentaries (shuruh)
B) Later fatwa collections
C) Reliable abridged texts (mutun)
D) The Qur'an and Sunnah

Key Takeaway
The mufti must balance textual hierarchy with deep juristic intuition, always preserving the status of Muslims and using rules as aids, not absolutes.

The Tenth Principle: Mafhum Mukhalif in Fiqh Books
Rule on validity of mafhum mukhalif in fiqh book expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a mafhum mukhalif can be relied upon in Hanafi fatwa and distinguish it from mafhum muwafaqah.

Core Idea
Mafhum mukhalif is valid in fiqh books but not in divine texts—a key distinction for the Hanafi mufti.

In this lesson, we explore a crucial principle for the Hanafi mufti: the validity of implied contrary meanings (mafhum mukhalif) in the expressions found in fiqh books. While such implications are generally not accepted as proof from the Qur'an and Sunnah in the Hanafi school, they become operative within the juristic corpus. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplication of usul rules when deriving fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish between mantuq and mafhum
Identify which part of an expression is explicitly stated (mantuq) and which is implied by something other than the word (mafhum). This is the first analytical step in parsing fiqh texts.
The mantuq is directly indicated by the word; the mafhum is inferred from the context.
2
Classify the mafhum type
Determine whether the implication agrees with the ruling of the mantuq (mafhum muwafaqah) or gives the opposite ruling (mafhum mukhalif). Only mafhum mukhalif is subject to the special rule under discussion.
Mafhum muwafaqah is accepted even in divine texts by Hanafis.
3
Apply the rule of the tenth principle
For a mafhum mukhalif, check the source: if it is from a fiqh book (not divine text), it may be relied upon. Then verify the condition: it must not contradict an explicit statement elsewhere in the book.
This is a practical rule for muftis, not a general usul principle.
4
Recognize the epistemological boundary
Understand that the Hanafi school rejects mafhum mukhalif in divine texts due to the principle that divine texts are general unless specified. This is a key difference from the Shafi'i school.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafi muftis will not use mafhum mukhalif from Qur'an to derive rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل العاشر
إن المفهوم المخالف، وإن كان غير معتبر في النصوص الشرعية، ولكنّه معتبر في عبارات كتب الفقه، فيصح العمل بمفهوم عبارات الكتب الفقهيّة، بشرط أن لا يكون ذلك المفهوم المخالف معارضاً لصريح العبارات الأخرى.
إعلم أن ما يدلّ عليه لفظ من ألفاظ العِبارة يسمّى "منطوقاً" لتلك العبارة، وما دلّ عليه شيء غير اللفظ المذكور في تلك العبارة يُسمّي "مفهوماً". ثمّ "المفهوم " علي قسمين:
الأول: "مفهوم الموافقة" وهو دلالة العبارة على ثبوت حكم المنطوق للمسكوت بمجرد فهم اللغة، أي بلا توقف علي رأي واجتهاد كدلالة قوله
تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَقُل هُمَا أُتِ [؟]﴾ [الإسراء : ۲۳] على تحريم الضرب والشتم.
والثاني: "مفهوم المخالفة" وهو دلالة العبارة علي ثبوت نقيض حكم المنطوق للمسكوت ، كقولنا: "في الإبل السائمة زكوة " فمفهومه المخالف
The Tenth Principle: Indeed, the implied contrary meaning (mafhum mukhalif), even if it is not considered valid in the divine texts, is considered valid in the expressions of fiqh books. So it is permissible to act upon the implied meaning of the expressions of fiqh books, on condition that this implied contrary meaning does not contradict the explicit expressions of other [texts]. Know that what is indicated by a word of the expression is called 'mantuq' (explicit meaning) of that expression, and what is indicated by something other than the mentioned word in that expression is called 'mafhum' (implied meaning). Then, 'mafhum' is of two types: First: 'mafhum muwafaqah' (consonant implication), which is the implication of the expression establishing the same ruling for the unstated case by mere understanding of the language, i.e., without depending on opinion and ijtihad, like the indication of the Almighty's saying: {So do not say to them 'uff'} [al-Isra 17:23] that hitting and abusing are prohibited. Second: 'mafhum mukhalif' (contrary implication), which is the implication of the expression establishing the opposite of the ruling of the stated case for the unstated case, like our saying: 'There is zakat on grazing camels'—its contrary implication is that there is no zakat on non-grazing camels.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage discusses a key principle in Hanafi usul al-iftā': the use of implied meanings (mafhum) in fiqh texts. Although in the primary sources (Qur'an and Sunnah) the mafhum mukhalif (contrary implication) is generally not considered a valid proof in the Hanafi school—as the Hanafi position is that the divine texts are not to be understood through such implications unless supported by context—in the secondary juristic literature (kutub al-fiqh), it is different. The mufti may rely on the mafhum mukhalif of expressions found in fiqh books, provided it does not conflict with explicit statements elsewhere. This is a practical concession for deriving rulings from the juristic corpus. The text then defines mantuq (explicit) and mafhum (implicit), and divides mafhum into two: mafhum muwafaqah (where the unstated case follows the same ruling as the stated case by a priority of meaning) and mafhum mukhalif (where the unstated case gets the opposite ruling, typically indicated by a condition, attribute, number, etc.). The example for muwafaqah is the Qur'anic verse: 'So do not say to them 'uff'' – this explicitly prohibits saying 'uff', but by implication it also prohibits hitting and scolding (since they are greater offenses). This is called daleel al-khitab in some terminologies. The example for mukhalif is 'on grazing camels zakat is due' – the explicit ruling is zakat on grazing camels; thus, by contrary implication, non-grazing camels (i.e., working camels) are not subject to zakat. The Hanafi school indeed distinguishes between grazing and non-grazing camels for zakat, based on this very implication, though the text notes it is valid only in fiqh books.

Key Terms
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit meaning indicated directly by the words of an expression.
مفهوم الموافقة (mafhum muwafaqah): Implication where the unstated case obtains the same ruling as the stated case by linguistic priority.
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum mukhalif): Implication where the unstated case obtains the opposite ruling of the stated case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tenth principle, when can a mufti rely on the mafhum mukhalif (contrary implication) from a fiqh book?
A) Always, without any condition
B) Only if it is supported by a Quranic verse
C) On condition that it does not contradict explicit statements in other texts
D) Only if it is from the works of Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may rely on the contrary implication (mafhum mukhalif) of an expression in a fiqh book, provided it does not conflict with any explicit statement elsewhere.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Mafhum al-Mukhalafah in Fiqh Works: A Hanafi Usul al-Iftaa Principle
Rule on using implicit contrary meaning from fiqh texts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mafhum al-mukhalafah is valid in fiqh books, identify its five types, and state the condition for its use.

Core Idea
Mafhum al-mukhalafah is valid in fiqh books, not in Quran/Sunnah — a practical tool for the Hanafi mufti.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, the implicit contrary meaning (mafhum al-mukhalafah) is not accepted as a proof in the Quran and Sunnah. However, when deriving rulings from compiled fiqh works, the Hanafi school does allow reliance on mafhum al-mukhalafah — provided it does not contradict an explicit statement elsewhere in the same book. This lesson parses the definitions, categories, and the crucial condition for its application in the context of iftaa.

Guided Path
1
Define manṭūq and mafhūm
Identify from the passage that manṭūq is what a word directly indicates, while mafhūm is what is understood from something other than the word itself.
This is the foundational terminological distinction.
2
Distinguish concordant and contrary implicit meaning
Mafhūm al-muwāfaqah agrees with the explicit ruling (e.g., prohibition of hitting from 'do not say uff'). Mafhūm al-mukhālafah gives the opposite ruling (e.g., no zakat on non-grazing camels). Note that only mafhūm al-mukhālafah is contested.
Mafhūm al-muwāfaqah is accepted by all schools; mafhūm al-mukhālafah is the subject of disagreement.
3
List the five types of mafhūm al-mukhālafah
Mafhūm al-ṣifah (adjective), mafhūm al-sharṭ (condition), mafhūm al-ghāyah (limit), mafhūm al-ʿadad (number), mafhūm al-laqab (proper noun). Memorize them with examples from the passage.
Each type arises from a specific linguistic feature in the statement.
4
Apply the condition for using mafhūm al-mukhālafah in fiqh books
The passage states that mafhūm al-mukhālafah from a fiqh book is valid only if it does not contradict an explicit statement (ṣarīḥ) elsewhere in the same book. This is a safety check to ensure consistency.
If contradiction occurs, the explicit statement overrides the implicit meaning.
5
Contrast Hanafi and Shafiʿi positions on primary texts
Hanafis do not accept mafhūm al-mukhālafah in Quran/Sunnah; Shafiʿis accept it (except mafhūm al-laqab). Understand the practical consequence: a Hanafi mufti cannot use mafhūm al-mukhālafah to derive a ruling directly from a hadith, but a Shafiʿi can.
This ikhtilaf is rooted in different usul principles about linguistic implication.

Source Text

الأصل العاشر
إن المفهوم المخالف، وإن كان غير معتبر في النصوص الشرعية، ولكنّه معتبر في عبارات كتب الفقه، فيصح العمل بمفهوم عبارات الكتب الفقهيّة، بشرط أن لا يكون ذلك المفهوم المخالف معارضاً لصريح العبارات الأخرى. إعلم أن ما يدلّ عليه لفظ من ألفاظ العِبارة يسمّى "منطوقاً" لتلك العبارة، وما دلّ عليه شيء غير اللفظ المذكور في تلك العبارة يُسمّي "مفهوماً". ثمّ "المفهوم " علي قسمين: الأول: "مفهوم الموافقة" وهو دلالة العبارة على ثبوت حكم المنطوق للمسكوت بمجرد فهم اللغة، أي بلا توقف علي رأي واجتهاد كدلالة قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا تَقُل هُمَا أُتِ ﴾ [الإسراء : ۲۳] على تحريم الضرب والشتم. والثاني: "مفهوم المخالفة" وهو دلالة العبارة علي ثبوت نقيض حكم المنطوق للمسكوت ، كقولنا: "في الإبل السائمة زكوة " فمفهومه المخالف أنه لا تجب الزكوة على الإبل العلوفة. ثمّ المفهوم المخالف ينقسم الي أقسام الأول: "مفهوم الصفة " وهو ما دلّ عليه لفظ وقع صفة لموصوف، كقولنا :" في الإبل السائمة زكوة". الثاني: "مفهوم الشرط " وهو ما دل علي انتفاء الحكم عند انتفاء الشرط، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِن كُنْ أُوْلَتِ حَمْلٍ فَأَنفِقُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ حَتَّى يَضَعْنَ حَمْلَهُنَّ [الطلاق : ٦] فمفهومه المخالف أنّ الإنفاق لا يجب علي المطلقة المبتوتة التي ليست حاملة. الثالث: "مفهوم الغاية" وهو ما دلّ على أن حكم المنطوق منتف فيما بعد الغاية، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَرْجُلَكُمْ إِلَى الْكَعْبَيْنِ ﴾ [المائدة : ٦] فإن مفهومه أن ما وراء الكعبين لا يجب غسله. الرابع: "مفهوم العدد" وهو ما دلّ على أنّ حكم المنطوق مقتصر على العدد الملفوظ، ويثبت نقيض ذلك الحكم علي ما وراء ذلك العدد. نحو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَيبِينَ جَلْدَةً ﴾ [النور: ٤] فإن مفهومه أنه لا يُجلك فوق ثمانين. الخامس: "مفهوم اللقب " وهو ما دلّ على أنّ حكم المنطوق مقتصر على الاسم الجامد المذكور فى العبارة، وأن نقيضه ثابت لغير ذلك الاسم الجامد. أما مثل قولنا: "في الغنم زكوة. " فإن مفهومه أنه ليس في غير الغنم زكوة. مفهوم الموافقة، فهو معتبر فى النصوص الشرعية وفي كتب الفقه جميعاً بالاتفاق. وأما المفهوم المخالف فى القرآن والسنة، ففى اعتباره خلاف فهو معتبر عند الشافعية بجميع أقسامه، سوى القسم الأخير وهو "مفهوم اللقب "، وعند الحنفية غير معتبر بمعنى أن النص لا يدل على
The Tenth Principle: Indeed the implicit contrary meaning (mafhum al-mukhalafah), even if it is not considered valid in the primary legal texts (nusus shar'iyyah), is nevertheless considered valid in the statements of fiqh books. So it is permissible to act upon the implicit meaning of the statements of fiqh books, on condition that that implicit contrary meaning does not contradict explicit statements. Know that what is indicated by a word from the words of an expression is called the 'explicit meaning' (mantuq) of that expression, and what is indicated by something other than the mentioned word in that expression is called the 'implicit meaning' (mafhum). Then 'implicit meaning' is of two types: First: 'implicit meaning of concordance' (mafhum al-muwafaqah) which is the indication of an expression of the establishment of the ruling of the explicit for the unmentioned merely by linguistic understanding, i.e. without depending on opinion and ijtihad, like the indication of His statement: {So do not say to them 'uff'} [al-Isra 17:23] to the prohibition of hitting and cursing. Second: 'implicit contrary meaning' (mafhum al-mukhalafah) which is the indication of an expression of the establishment of the opposite of the ruling of the explicit for the unmentioned, like our saying: 'On grazing camels there is zakat' – its implicit contrary meaning is that zakat is not obligatory on fed camels. Then the implicit contrary meaning is divided into divisions. First: 'implicit meaning of adjective' (mafhum al-sifah) – what is indicated by a word that occurs as an adjective for a described noun, like our saying: 'On grazing camels there is zakat.' Second: 'implicit meaning of condition' (mafhum al-shart) – what indicates the negation of the ruling upon the negation of the condition, like His statement: {And if they are pregnant, then spend on them until they give birth to their pregnancy} [al-Talaq 65:6] – its implicit contrary meaning is that spending is not obligatory on an irrevocably divorced woman who is not pregnant. Third: 'implicit meaning of limit' (mafhum al-ghayah) – what indicates that the ruling of the explicit is negated beyond the limit, like His statement: {And your feet to the ankles} [al-Ma'ida 5:6] – its implicit meaning is that beyond the ankles washing is not obligatory. Fourth: 'implicit meaning of number' (mafhum al-'adad) – what indicates that the ruling of the explicit is restricted to the stated number, and the opposite of that ruling is established for beyond that number, like His statement: {Then flog them eighty lashes} [al-Nur 24:4] – its implicit meaning is that one does not flog above eighty. Fifth: 'implicit meaning of proper noun' (mafhum al-laqab) – what indicates that the ruling of the explicit is restricted to the inert noun mentioned in the expression, and its opposite is established for other than that inert noun, like our saying: 'On sheep there is zakat' – its implicit meaning is that there is no zakat on other than sheep. As for the implicit meaning of concordance, it is considered valid in the primary legal texts and in fiqh books unanimously. And as for the implicit contrary meaning in the Quran and Sunnah, there is disagreement concerning its validity: it is considered valid according to the Shafi'is in all its divisions except the last division, which is 'mafhum al-laqab', and according to the Hanafis it is not considered valid – meaning that the text does not indicate...
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth principle in the summary of rules for the mufti. The author, Muhammad Taqi Usmani, clarifies that while mafhum al-mukhalafah (implicit contrary meaning) is not recognized as a valid proof in the Quran and Sunnah according to the Hanafi school, it is still operative in the statements of fiqh books. This means that a mufti can rely on mafhum al-mukhalafah derived from a fiqh text (e.g., 'in grazing camels there is zakat' implies no zakat on non-grazing camels) to issue a fatwa, provided it does not contradict an explicit statement in another part of the fiqh work. The passage then defines 'manṭūq' (explicit) and 'mafhūm' (implicit), and divides mafhūm into mafhūm al-muwāfaqah (implicit concordant meaning) and mafhūm al-mukhālafah (implicit contrary meaning). It lists five categories of mafhūm al-mukhālafah: adjective, condition, limit, number, and proper noun. The Hanafi position is that mafhūm al-mukhālafah is not a proof in the primary texts (Quran and Hadith), but it is considered valid in fiqh compilations as a practical tool for deriving rulings. The Shafiʿi school, by contrast, accepts mafhūm al-mukhālafah in the primary texts except for mafhūm al-laqab. This distinction is crucial for a mufti: when extracting rulings from a fiqh book, he may use mafhūm al-mukhālafah, but when interpreting a Quranic verse or hadith, he should not rely on it according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
منطوق (manṭūq): The explicit meaning indicated directly by the words of an expression.
مفهوم الموافقة (mafhūm al-muwāfaqah): An implicit meaning that is in agreement with the explicit ruling; the omitted item takes the same ruling due to a stronger or equal reason.
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafah): An implicit meaning that contradicts the explicit ruling; the omitted item takes the opposite ruling due to the qualification mentioned.
مفهوم الصفة (mafhūm al-ṣifah): Implicit meaning derived from an adjective or descriptive phrase, implying that the ruling is limited to the described state.
مفهوم الشرط (mafhūm al-sharṭ): Implicit meaning derived from a conditional clause, implying that the ruling ceases when the condition is absent.
مفهوم الغاية (mafhūm al-ghāyah): Implicit meaning derived from a term denoting a limit, implying that the ruling does not apply beyond that limit.
مفهوم العدد (mafhūm al-ʿadad): Implicit meaning derived from a specified number, implying that the ruling is restricted to that number.
مفهوم اللقب (mafhūm al-laqab): Implicit meaning derived from a proper noun or a specific name, implying that the ruling is exclusive to that named entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a condition for acting upon mafhum al-mukhalafah derived from a fiqh book?
A) It must be supported by a consensus (ijma').
B) It must not contradict an explicit statement in the same book.
C) It must be from the Quran or Sunnah.
D) It must be approved by a living mufti.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-mukhalafah is a valid interpretive tool in Hanafi fiqh books, but only when it does not contradict an explicit statement in the same work.

Mafhum al-Mukhalafa in Primary Texts vs. Fiqh Books
Explaining the limitation of mafhum al-mukhalafa in Quran/Sunnah vs. its acceptance in fiqh books

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that mafhum al-mukhalafa is operative in fiqh texts but not necessarily in primary Shariah sources, and identify when a specification in a text is a genuine restriction versus a rhetorical flourish.

Core Idea
A specification in a primary text may be rhetorical, not restrictive; only in fiqh books is the opposite implication binding.

The Hanafi school makes a crucial distinction between the language of the Quran and Sunnah, which often contains rhetorical elements, and the precise legal language of fiqh works. Understanding when a specification creates an opposite ruling—and when it does not—is essential for the mufti. This lesson explains that principle through the example of mourning (ihdad) and clarifies the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i critique.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the hadith and its explicit condition
Read the hadith: it prohibits mourning beyond three days for 'a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day', except for a husband. The condition is the woman's faith.
The explicit condition is 'believing woman'.
2
Examine the Hanafi inference regarding those not mentioned
Hanafis hold that minor and dhimmi women are not obligated because they are not addressed; the silence does not obligate them. They revert to the original principle (istishab) of no mourning obligation.
This is not mafhum al-mukhalafa but a failure of address.
3
Understand the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response
Shafi'is treat the specification as mafhum al-mukhalafa, obligating the opposite for those not mentioned. Hanafis respond that in primary texts, such specifications may be rhetorical, not restrictive.
The dispute is over the nature of the specification: genuine restriction vs. rhetorical emphasis.
4
Distinguish between primary texts and fiqh works
Quran and Sunnah may contain emphasis, rebuke, or exhortation, which do not create legal restrictions. Fiqh books use precise legal language, so mafhum al-mukhalafa applies there.
The difference lies in the purpose and style of the text.
5
Apply the rule to Quranic examples
Quranic phrases like 'small price' (Q.2:41) and 'doubled and multiplied' (Q.3:130) are rhetorical, not legal conditions. They do not permit the opposite.
This reinforces the principle that context matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي نقيض الحكم لغير المنطوق، فيبقى المفهوم مسكوتاً عنه، فإن دل دليل على أنّ حكمه حكم المنطوق، عُمِل به، وإن دل دليل على أن حكمه مناقض لحكم المنطوق عمل به ومما يدل على ذلك أن المسكوت يبقى على أصله، فإن كان الأصل نقيضاً لحكم المنطوق ثبت انتفاء الحكم في المسكوت، لا لكون المفهوم معتبراً، بل لبقاء المسكوت على الأصل. مثاله: ماورد عن النبي الكريم صلى الله عليه وسلّم: "لاَيَحِلُّ لاِمْرَأَةٍ تُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ، تُحِدُّ (۱) " عَلَى مَيْتٍ فَوْقَ ثَلَاثِ إِلا عَلَى زَوْجِ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْهُرٍ وَعَشْراً فإنّ حكم الإحداد على الزوج في الحديث مقتصر على امرأة مؤمنة. ولذلك ذهب الحنفية إلى أنه لا يجب الإحداد على الصغيرة والذمية، خلافاً للشافعية. وزعم الحافظ ابن حجر رحمه الله تعالى أن استدلال الحنفية بهذا الحديث استدلال بالمفهوم على خلاف ما أصلوة والحق أنه ليس استدلالاً بالمفهوم، بل الخطاب في الحديث إنّما وُجّه إلى امرأةٍ مؤمنة. فأمّا الصغيرة والدمية، فقد سكت الحديث عن خطابها، فترجعان إلى أصلهما، وهو عدم وجوب الإحداد، لأن وجوب الإحداد لابد له من دليل، ولا دليل ههنا. وأما في كتب الفقه، فمفهوم المخالفة معتبر عند الحنفية أيضاً، وكذلك فى المعاملات الجارية بين النّاس. ووجه الفرق بين النصوص الشرعية والعبارات الفقهيّة أنّ نصوص القرآن والسنّة تحتوى على عبارات بليغة حكيمة، فربما تُذكر فيها ألفاظ للتأكيد، أو التوبيخ والتشنيع، أو الوعظ والتذكير (۱) الحديث أخرجه الشيخان وهذا اللفظ لمسلم، باب وجوب الإحداد في عدة الوفاة، حديث ۳۷۰٦. ولا تكون قيداً لما سبق كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَشْتَرُوا بِنَايَنِي ثَمَنًا قَلِيلاً) [البقرة : ٤١] فإنما أضيف لفظ "قليلاً" للتشنيع على هذا العمل، ولا يدل على أن الاشتراء بالثّمن الكثير جائز. وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تَأْكُلُوا الرَّبوا أَضْعَيفًا مُضَعَفَةٌ [آل عمران: ۱۳۰] فإنّه لا يدل على جواز الربوا إذا لم يكن ضعف الأصل. . أما كتب الفقه، فإنّ مقصودها تدوين الأحكام على طريقة قانونية، وليس فيها شيئ من التأكيد والتشنيع وغير ذلك، فلا بد من اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة فيها. فماثبت بمفهومها المخالف يؤخذ به، إلا إذا كان معارضاً لمنطوق عبارة أخرى.
Summary of the rules for the Mufti: The opposite (contradictory) ruling is for what is not explicitly stated; the implied meaning remains unaddressed. If evidence indicates that its ruling is the same as the explicit ruling, it is acted upon. If evidence indicates that its ruling contradicts the explicit ruling, it is acted upon. Evidence for this is that the unaddressed remains on its original principle. If the original principle is the opposite of the explicit ruling, then the negation of the ruling is established for the unaddressed, not because the implied meaning is considered, but because the unaddressed remains on the original principle. Example: What is narrated from the noble Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to mourn (i.e., observe iddah mourning) for a deceased person for more than three days, except for her husband (for) four months and ten days.' The ruling of mourning for the husband in this hadith is limited to a believing woman. Therefore, the Hanafis held that mourning is not obligatory for a minor or a dhimmi woman, contrary to the Shafi'is. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, may Allah have mercy on him, claimed that the Hanafis' inference from this hadith is an inference by implied meaning contrary to their principle. The truth is that it is not inference by implied meaning; rather, the address in the hadith is directed to a believing woman. As for the minor and the dhimmi woman, the hadith is silent about addressing them, so they revert to their original principle, which is the non-obligation of mourning, because the obligation of mourning necessarily requires evidence, and there is no evidence here. As for fiqh books, the implied opposite meaning is considered according to the Hanafis as well, and similarly in transactions among people. The difference between sharia texts and juristic expressions is that the texts of the Quran and Sunnah contain eloquent and wise expressions; sometimes words are used for emphasis, or for rebuke and denunciation, or for exhortation and reminder, and they are not restrictions for what preceded. For example, the Almighty's saying: 'And do not exchange My signs for a small price' [Al-Baqarah: 41]; the word 'small' is added to denounce this action, and it does not indicate that buying for a large price is permissible. Likewise, the Almighty's saying: 'Do not consume usury, doubled and multiplied' [Aal-e-Imran: 130]; it does not indicate permissibility of usury if it is not doubled. As for fiqh books, their purpose is to codify rulings in a legal manner, and there is nothing of emphasis, denunciation, etc., so it is necessary to consider the implied opposite meaning in them. So what is established by its opposite implication is accepted, unless it is contradicted by the explicit statement of another expression.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi position on mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) and how it differs between primary Shariah texts (Quran and Sunnah) and secondary fiqh works. The author clarifies that in the primary texts, wording often includes rhetorical elements such as emphasis, rebuke, or exhortation, which are not intended as legal restrictions. Hence, one cannot automatically infer the opposite ruling from such texts. The example of mourning (ihdad) illustrates this: the hadith specifies 'a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day,' but the Hanafis argue that the silence of the hadith regarding minor and dhimmi women does not create an opposite implication; rather, those women revert to the original principle that mourning is not obligatory for them. In contrast, in fiqh books where the language is legal and precise, mafhum al-mukhalafa is operative. The author also addresses the critique of Ibn Hajar, asserting that the Hanafi inference is not based on mafhum al-mukhalafa but on the absence of address. The passage is an expansion probe into a rasm rule for muftis: understanding when opposite implication is valid and when it is not.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The opposite implication (concept of opposition) from a qualified statement; that the ruling applies to the opposite case.
منطوق (mantuq): What is explicitly stated in the text.
مسكوت (maskut): What is not explicitly stated but left unaddressed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi perspective explained in this passage, why is it that a dhimmi (non-Muslim) woman is not obligated to observe mourning (ihdad) for her husband based on the hadith?
A) Because the hadith does not address her, and she returns to the original principle of non-obligation.
B) Because the concept of opposite implication requires that women not mentioned are prohibited from mourning.
C) Because the hadith is weak and cannot be used as evidence.
D) Because the hadith specifically permits it for dhimmi women.

Key Takeaway
The opposite implication (mafhum al-mukhalafa) is binding only in fiqh texts where language is precise; in primary Shariah texts, rhetorical flourishes may break the implication.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate

The Tenth Rule: Mafhum al-Mukhalafa in Fiqh Books
Explains when mafhum al-mukhalafa applies vs rhetorical context

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rhetorical and legal contexts for qualifying phrases and apply the rule that mafhum al-mukhalafa is binding in fiqh books unless contradicted by an explicit text.

Core Idea
In fiqh books, every qualifying description is a condition; in the Quran, it is often rhetorical.

This lesson introduces the tenth rule of Rasm al-Mufti: the concept of mafhum al-mukhalafa and when it is binding. Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani explains that while the Quran uses qualifying phrases for rhetorical condemnation, fiqh texts are legal codifications where such phrases must be taken as deliberate restrictions. Understanding this distinction prevents misapplication of Quranic verses as proof for permissibility and ensures consistent fatwa derivation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Quranic examples
Analyze the two Quranic verses cited: 'Do not exchange My verses for a small price' and 'Do not consume usury multiplied.' The words 'small' and 'multiplied' are used for rhetorical condemnation, not as legal conditions.
In Quranic discourse, such phrases aim to emphasize the gravity of the act, not to define its scope.
2
Recognize the difference in purpose
Fiqh books are codified legal texts where every phrase is intended to precisely define the ruling. Thus, qualifications in fiqh are assumed to be conditions unless proven otherwise.
This principle guided the Hanafi school's method of deriving fiqh from legal manuals.
3
Apply mafhum al-mukhalafa in fiqh texts
For a fiqh statement like 'The sale of gharar is prohibited,' the qualification 'gharar' creates a mafhum al-mukhalafa: sales without gharar are permissible.
This inference holds unless another explicit text (mantuq) contradicts it.
4
Identify the exception
If the mafhum al-mukhalafa conflicts with an explicit text (mantuq) from another source, the explicit text takes precedence.
This ensures the rule does not override clear evidence.
5
Synthesize the rule for fatwa
A mufti must first determine if the text is from a fiqh book or a rhetorical source. If it is fiqh, apply mafhum al-mukhalafa unless contradicted. If it is Quranic or rhetorical, the description is not necessarily restrictive.
This rule is a cornerstone of Hanafi iftaa methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول الإفتاء
تلخيص قواعد رسم المفتي ولا تكون قيداً لما سبق كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلا تَشْتَرُوا بِآيَاتِي ثَمَنًا قَلِيلاً﴾ [البقرة: ٤١] فإنما أضيف لفظ "قليلاً" للتشنيع على هذا العمل، ولا يدل على أن الاشتراء بالثّمن الكثير جائز. وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿لَا تَأْكُلُوا الرِّبَا أَضْعَافًا مُضَاعَفَةً﴾ [آل عمران: ۱۳۰] فإنّه لا يدل على جواز الربا إذا لم يكن ضعف الأصل. أما كتب الفقه، فإنّ مقصودها تدوين الأحكام على طريقة قانونية، وليس فيها شيء من التأكيد والتشنيع وغير ذلك، فلا بد من اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة فيها. فما ثبت بمفهومها المخالف يؤخذ به، إلا إذا كان معارضاً لمنطوق عبارة أخرى.
Principles of Issuing Fatwa
Summary of the Rules of the Mufti's Manual: 'And it [the attribute] is not a restriction for what preceded, like His statement: 'And do not exchange My verses for a small price' [al-Baqarah 2:41]; the word 'small' was added only to condemn this action, and it does not indicate that purchasing for a large price is permissible. Similarly, His statement: 'Do not consume usury multiplied' [Aal 'Imran 3:130]; it does not indicate that usury is permissible if it is not multiplied. As for fiqh books, their purpose is to codify rulings in a legal manner, and there is nothing of emphasis, condemnation, etc. in them. Therefore, it is necessary to consider the concept of contrary in them. So whatever is established by its contrary concept is taken, unless it conflicts with the explicit text of another expression.'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
Passage type: Rasm rule (الأصل العاشر) concerning the application of mafhum al-mukhalafa (concept of contrary) in fiqh texts. The author explains that in the Quran, descriptive phrases are often used for rhetorical emphasis, not to establish legal conditions. For example, the verse 'Do not exchange My verses for a small price' uses 'small' to condemn the act, not to permit a large price. Similarly, 'Do not consume usury multiplied' does not permit usury that is not multiplied. However, fiqh books are legal codifications, not rhetorical texts. Therefore, any qualifying description in a fiqh ruling creates a mafhum al-mukhalafa that restricts the ruling to that description, unless it contradicts an explicit statement elsewhere.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): The concept of contrary; understanding from a qualified expression that the ruling differs when the qualification is absent.
منطوق (mantuq): The explicit text or spoken expression of a ruling.
التشنيع (tashnī'): Rhetorical condemnation; the use of exaggerated language to criticize an action, not to establish a legal condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the tenth rule, in which type of text is mafhum al-mukhalafa applicable?
A) The Quran
B) Hadith
C) Fiqh books
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The tenth rule establishes that in fiqh books, qualifying descriptions create binding mafhum al-mukhalafa, unlike the Quran where they are often rhetorical.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Prohibition of Weak Rulings Except for Necessity
Rasm al-Mufti rule with ijma proof and necessity example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a mufti may act on a weak or marjuh opinion and apply the rule to a concrete fiqh scenario.

Core Idea
Acting on weak or marjuh opinions is prohibited by ijma unless genuine necessity arises and the mufti is deeply learned.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle of Hanafi iftaa: a muqallid mufti must adhere to the validated opinions of the madhhab and cannot freely choose weak or marjuh rulings. However, an exception exists for cases of necessity, provided the mufti is qualified to recognize such necessity. We will examine the rule, its basis in ijma, and a practical example from Ibn Abidin regarding ghusl.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the core prohibition: it is not permissible to act upon or issue fatwa with weak (da'if) or preponderated (marjuh) narrations or opinions.
The rule applies to both the mufti's own practice and his fatwa.
2
Understand the basis in ijma
Analyze the quote from Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: acting on a marjuh opinion is contrary to consensus; the marjuh is like non-existent compared to the rajih.
This establishes that the rule is not merely recommended but binding by consensus.
3
Recognize the exception for necessity
Identify the conditions for the exception: genuine necessity (darurah) and the mufti must be mutabahhir (deeply learned) to discern when necessity applies.
The necessity cannot be based on whim; it must be a compelling situation.
4
Apply the exception to the ghusl example
Walk through the scenario: the majority opinion requires ghusl even if desire subsided, but Abu Yusuf's marjuh view does not. Necessity (fear of suspicion while traveling) allows following Abu Yusuf's view.
This shows how the exception works in practice: it permits the individual to act on the weak opinion for himself, not for general fatwa.
5
Distinguish mufta bihi and necessity-based fatwa
Note that the relied-upon position remains the majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). The weak opinion is not elevated to general practice; it is only used in the specific necessity case.
The mufti must clearly distinguish between the general fatwa and the exceptional permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الحادي عشر
لا يجوز العمل أو الإفتاء بالروايات الضعيفة أو المرجوحة، إلا لضرورة تبدو لمفت عارف متبحر.
قدمنا أن الواجب على المفتي المقلد أن يأخذ من الأقوال والروايات ما صححها أصحاب الترجيح. وأما ما يوجد في كتب الفقه من أقوال وروايات ضعيفة صرح أصحاب الترجيح بضعفها، أو علم ضعفها بعباراتهم ضمناً والتزاماً، فلا يجوز العمل عليها والإفتاء بها. وقال العلامة قاسم بن قطلوبغا رحمه الله تعالى: "إن الحكم والفتيا بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع، وإن المرجوح في مقابلة الراجح بمنزلة العدم، والترجيح بغير مرجح في المتقابلات ممنوع، وإن من يكتفى بأن يكون فتواه أو عمله موافقاً لقول أو وجه في المسألة، ويعمل بما شاء من الأقوال والوجوه من غير نظر في الترجيح، فقد جهل وخرق الإجماع".
ولكن صرح عدة من الفقهاء بأنه قد يجوز العمل أو الإفتاء برواية ضعيفة أو قول مرجوح لضرورة اقتضت ذلك. وحاصل كلامهم أنه لا يجوز الأخذ بالأقوال الضعيفة بالتشهي، ولكن إذا ابتلي الرجل بحاجة ملحة، وسع له أن يعمل لنفسه بقول ضعيف أو رواية مرجوحة. وقد ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين في شرح عقود رسم المفتي "عدة أمثلة لهذه الحاجة:
الأول: المذهب المفتى به عند الحنفية أن المني إذا انفصل عن مقره بشهوة يجب الغسل، سواء كانت الشهوة فترت عند خروجه من الآلة أم لا، فلو أمسك رجل ذكره عندما أحس بالاحتلام إلى أن فترت شهوته، ثم أرسله، فخرج المني بعد فتورها وجب الغسل عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى لا يجب الغسل إلا إذا كانت الشهوة باقية عند الخروج. وقد أفتى أصحاب الترجيح بقول الطرفين، فصار قول أبي يوسف لا يعمل به. ولكن إذا كان الرجل مسافراً أو كان ضيفاً عند رجال يخاف عليه الريبة، وسع له في مثل ذلك أن يعمل بقول أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى.
The Eleventh Principle: It is not permissible to act or issue fatwa based on weak or preponderated (marjuh) narrations, except for a necessity that appears to a knowledgeable, deeply learned mufti. We have already stated that the duty of a muqallid mufti is to take from the statements and narrations what the scholars of tarjih have validated. As for what is found in fiqh books of weak statements and narrations that the scholars of tarjih have explicitly declared weak, or whose weakness is known implicitly from their expressions and commitments, it is not permissible to act upon them or issue fatwa with them. Allama Qasim bin Qutlubugha (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Indeed, judging and giving fatwa with what is marjuh is contrary to consensus, and the marjuh in comparison to the rajih is like non-existence, and tarjih without a preponderating factor in conflicting matters is prohibited, and whoever is content that his fatwa or action agrees with a statement or aspect in the issue, and acts upon whichever statements and aspects he pleases without regard to tarjih, has indeed shown ignorance and broken consensus.' However, several jurists have stated that it may be permissible to act or give fatwa based on a weak narration or marjuh statement due to a necessity that requires it. The gist of their words is that it is not permissible to adopt weak statements out of whim, but if a person is afflicted with an urgent need, it is expanded for him to act for himself based on a weak statement or a marjuh narration. Allama Ibn Abidin mentioned in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti several examples of this need: First: The relied-upon madhhab among the Hanafis is that if mani separates from its source with desire, ghusl is obligatory, regardless of whether the desire subsided at the time of exiting the organ or not. If a man held his penis when he felt the onset of nocturnal emission until his desire subsided, then released it, and the mani came out after the subsidence, ghusl is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said ghusl is not obligatory unless the desire remained at the time of exit. The scholars of tarjih issued fatwa with the saying of both sides, so Abu Yusuf's saying is not acted upon. However, if a man is traveling or is a guest among men where he fears suspicion, it is expanded for him in such a case to act according to the saying of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
Passage type: Rasm rule (الأصل الحادي عشر) regarding the prohibition of acting on weak or preponderated (marjuh) opinions, with an exception for necessity. The rule states that a muqallid mufti must only use opinions that the scholars of tarjih have validated. Opinions explicitly declared weak or known to be weak are not permissible for practice or fatwa. The author quotes Allama Qasim ibn Qutlubugha who states that acting on a marjuh opinion is contrary to ijma, and that the marjuh is like non-existent against the rajih. However, many jurists allow acting on weak opinions in cases of necessity, provided it is not out of whim. The mufti must be qualified (mutabahhir) to recognize the necessity. Then the first example from Ibn Abidin is given: The relied-upon Hanafi position on ghusl for mani is that ghusl is required even if the sexual desire subsides before exit, contrary to Abu Yusuf. But if a man is traveling or a guest in a compromising situation, he may follow Abu Yusuf's opinion on necessity. The second example begins but continues on the next page.

Key Terms
رواية ضعيفة (riwaya da'ifa): A narration or transmission that is weak in authenticity, as determined by scholars of hadith or fiqh tarjih.
قول مرجوح (qawl marjuh): A legal opinion that is preponderated over by a stronger opinion within the madhhab.
ضرورة (darurah): A necessity that justifies departure from the normal ruling, such as fear of suspicion or hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first example of the eleventh rule, what condition allows a person to act on Abu Yusuf's opinion about ghusl?
A) He is a scholar
B) He is traveling or in a suspicious situation
C) He is a mufti
D) He does not have water

Key Takeaway
A mufti must only use validated opinions; weak opinions are permissible only in genuine necessity, and only for the individual's case, not as a general fatwa.
