Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Acting on Weak Opinions in Necessity
Explains rule and examples for using weak opinions in dire need

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that weak (marjuh) opinions may be followed in necessity, distinguishing genuine necessity from mere convenience, and identify the conditions for later compensation.

Core Idea
Weak opinions are not for casual use; only dire necessity permits acting on them, often with later repetition.

A mufti must ordinarily issue fatwa based on the strongest, most relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi). However, the Hanafi tradition recognizes that pressing need (darurah) can make it permissible for an individual to follow a weak or outweighed opinion temporarily. This lesson unpacks that principle through the maxim 'يجوز العمل بالقول الضعيف عند الضرورة' and its applications in purification matters.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim and Its Scope
Begin by articulating the qawida: 'It is permissible to act upon a weak opinion in necessity.' Note that it governs both fatwa and personal practice in all fiqh chapters where hardship arises. Identify its rank as a minor maxim (sughra) that restricts the general prohibition of following weak opinions.
The restriction is 'لا يجوز الأخذ بالقول الضعيف مطلقاً إلا لضرورة' – no absolute adoption of weak opinions except for necessity.
2
Analyse the First Fur': Wet Dream and Ghusl
Apply the maxim to the case of a man who holds his penis until desire subsides, then releases semen. The strong view (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) requires ghusl; Abu Yusuf's weak view exempts it. In travel or among suspicious people, following the weak view is permitted due to hardship.
The mufta bihi remains the strong view, but the individual may act on the weak one for himself.
3
Analyse the Second Fur': Cauterization and Wudu
Now consider the case of blood from cauterization that wipes away but does not flow. The strong view: if wiping would cause flow, wudu breaks. A weak view from al-Hidayah says it does not. Ibn Abidin used this weak view when undergoing cauterization to pray without hardship, then later repeated the prayers.
This shows the temporary nature of the dispensation and the requirement to make up missed obligations if possible.
4
Identify the Istithna' (Exception)
The maxim has an exception: when there is no necessity, one must revert to the strong, relied-upon opinion. The default is 'الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان' – the original ruling remains in force.
This prevents abuse of the dispensation.
5
Evaluate the Practical Application for a Mufti
A mufti must distinguish between issuing a fatwa for the public (which stays on the mufta bihi) and advising an individual in hardship. The mufti may point to the weak opinion as a personal concession, but should not elevate it to the general fatwa.
This aligns with the adab of the mufti and the hierarchy of rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد جهل وخَرَق الإجماع "[1]"
ولكن صرّح عدة من الفقهاء بأنه قد يجوز العمل أو الإفتاء برواية ضعيفة أو قول مرجوح لضرورة اقتضت ذلك. وحاصل كلامهم أنه لا يجوز الأخذ بالأقوال الضعيفة بالتشهي، ولكن إذا ابتلي الرّجل بحاجة ملحة، وسع له أن يعمل لنفسه بقول ضعيف أو روايةٍ مرجوحة. وقد ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين في شرح عقود رسم المفتى "عدة أمثلة لهذه الحاجة:
الأوّل: المذهب المفتى به عند الحنفيّة أنّ المني إذا انفصل عن مَقَرَّه بشهوة يجب الغسل، سواء كانت الشهوةُ فَتَرَتْ عند خروجه من الآلة أم لا، فلو أمسك رجل ذكره عندما أحس بالاحتلام إلى أن فَتَرت شهوته، ثمّ أرسله، فخرج المني بعد فتورها وجبَ الغُسل عند أبي حنيفة و محمد رحمهما الله تعالى، وقال أبو يوسف رحمه الله تعالى لا يجب الغسل إلا إذا كانت الشهوة باقية عند الخروج. وقد أفتى أصحاب الترجيح بقول الطرفين، فصار قول أبي يوسف لا يُعمل به. ولكن إذا كان الرّجل مسافراً أو كان ضيفاً عند رجال يخاف عليه الرّيبة، وسعَ له في مثل ذلك أن يعمل بقول أبي يوسف رحمه الله تعالى.
الثاني: المذهب المفتى به عند الحنفيّة أنّ الدم إن ظهر بقشر نفطة، إن سال عن رأس الجرح نقض الوضوء، وإن لم يسيل لم ينقض والسيلان أن ينحدر عن رأس الجُرح. وإن علا على رأس الجرح وانتفخ ولم ينحدر، لم يكن سائلاً، وإن كان أكثر من رأس الجرح. وفي هذه الحالة إن مسحه الرّجل بخرقةٍ بحيث لو تركه ،سال، فإنّه ناقض للوضوء. ولكن هناك قول ضعيف[1] نقله صاحب الهداية بأنّ ذلك ليس بناقض، وهذا قول شاد مرجوح. ولكن ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أنه يسوغ للمعذور تقليد هذا القول عند الضرورة، وأنه كان قد ابتلي مرةً بكي الحمصة ولم يجد ما تصح به صلاته على مذهب الحنفيّة بغير مشقة شديدة إلا على هذا القول. ويقول العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "فاضطررت إلى تقليد هذا القول، ثمّ لما عافانى الله تعالى منه أعدت صلوة تلك المدة "[2]
وكذلك ذكر ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى في "البحر "أقوالاً ضعيفةً في بحث ألوان الدماء، ثم قال : "وفى معراج الدراية [3] مغزيّاً إلى فخر الأئمة[4]: لو أفتى

[1] رسائل ابن عابدین الفوائد المخصصة بأحكام كي الحمصة ١:٥٤
[2] شرح عقود رسم المفتى ص ۹۲
[3] معراج الدراية إلى شرح الهداية للشيخ الإمام قوام الدين محمد بن محمد البخاري الكاكي، المتوفى: سنة ٧٤٩، تسع وأربعين وسبعمائة فرغ من تأليفه : في ۲۱، إحدى وعشرين مجرم سنة ٧٤٥، وأربعين وسبعمائة ذكر فيه : أنه أراد بعد فقدان كتبه أن يجمع الفرائد من فوائد المشايخ والشارحين ليكون ذلك المجموع كالشرح، وبين فيه أقوال الأئمة الأربعة من الصحيح والأصح والمختار والجديد والقديم ووجه تمسكهم. كشف الظنون - ٢ / ٢٠٢٢) بتصرف يسير)
[4] محمد بن علي بن سعيد أبو بكر المطرزي البخاري المشهور بفخر الأئمة، الجواهر المضيئة للقرشى (٣ / (٢٦٠) وهو من علماء القرن السادس، أستاذ الإمام شرف الدين عمر بن محمد بن عمر العقيلي المتوفى سنة ست وسبعين وخمس مائة (٥٧٥(٥) الجواهر المضيئة ج ۲ ص ٦٦٧).
He has been ignorant and breached consensus. But several jurists have explicitly stated that it may be permissible to act or give fatwa based on a weak transmission or outweighed opinion due to a necessity that required that. The gist of their speech is that it is not permissible to adopt weak opinions out of desire, but if a person is afflicted with a pressing need, it is expansive for him to act for himself according to a weak opinion or an outweighed transmission. Allama Ibn Abidin mentioned in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti several examples of this need: First: The relied-upon madhhab among the Hanafis is that if semen separates from its place with desire, ghusl is obligatory, whether the desire subsided at its exit from the organ or not. So if a man holds his penis when he feels a wet dream until his desire subsides, then releases it, and semen comes out after the subsiding, ghusl is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) said: ghusl is not obligatory unless the desire remains at the time of exit. The proponents of tarjih have given fatwa with both views, so the view of Abu Yusuf is not acted upon. But if the man is travelling or is a guest among men who fear suspicion for him, it is expansive for him in such a case to act upon the view of Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him). Second: The relied-upon madhhab among the Hanafis is that if blood appears on a blister, if it flows from the head of the wound, it breaks wudu, and if it does not flow, it does not break it. Flowing is that it descends from the head of the wound. If it rises over the head of the wound and swells and does not descend, it is not flowing even if it is more than the head of the wound. In this case, if the man wipes it with a cloth such that if he left it, it would flow, then it breaks wudu. But there is a weak opinion transmitted by the author of al-Hidayah that this does not break wudu, and this is a deviant outweighed opinion. But Allama Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned that it is permissible for the excused to follow this opinion in necessity, and that he was once afflicted with cauterization of a chickpea (ki al-himmasa) and did not find anything by which his prayer could be valid according to the Hanafi madhhab without severe hardship except on this opinion. Allama Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) says: 'So I was forced to follow this opinion, then when Allah cured me of it, I repeated the prayers of that period.' Similarly, Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in al-Bahr weak opinions in the discussion of colors of blood, then said: 'And in Miraj al-Dirayah, referencing Fakhr al-A'imma: if one gives fatwa...'
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from the summary of the rules of the mufti addresses a key principle: weak (da'if) or outweighed (marjuh) opinions are not to be followed casually. However, a genuine necessity (darurah) can make it permissible for an individual to act on such an opinion for himself, though ideally the fatwa remains on the stronger view. The author presents two concrete examples from Ibn Abidin. The first deals with ghusl after a wet dream where the desire subsides before emission; Abu Yusuf's minority view is that ghusl is not required, but the madhhab's fatwa is against it. Nevertheless, in situations like travel or staying among suspicious people, one may adopt Abu Yusuf's view to avoid hardship. The second example concerns blood from a blister breaking wudu. The weak opinion from al-Hidayah says it does not break wudu even if it would flow if wiped, but this is rejected. Yet Ibn Abidin relates his own experience of undergoing a cauterization treatment (ki al-himmasa) where the only way to pray without difficulty was to follow that weak view; he did so, then later repeated the prayers after recovery. This shows the stance: in dire need, one may follow a weak opinion temporarily, but then it is necessary to make up for any missed obligations later. The passage underscores that necessity (darurah) does not make the weak opinion the primary fatwa, but it provides a personal dispensation.

Key Terms
قول ضعيف (qawl da'if): An opinion that is outweighed in evidence and not chosen for fatwa in the madhhab, but may be followed in necessity.
رسم المفتي (rasm al-mufti): The code of conduct and rules that a mufti must follow when issuing fatwas, including when to use weak opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition is it permissible to act upon a weak (da'if) opinion according to this passage?
A) Whenever the weak opinion is easier to follow.
B) Only when one is in a state of extreme necessity (darurah).
C) Only when the weak opinion is supported by a hadith.
D) At any time, because all opinions in the madhhab are valid.

Key Takeaway
A weak opinion may be followed individually in genuine necessity, but the mufta bihi remains the strong view; the dispensation is temporary and often requires later compensation.

6 min
Conditions for Acting on Weak Opinions in Necessity
Summarizing rules on when weak opinions may be followed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two scenarios in which a weak opinion (marjuh) may be followed in Hanafi fatwa practice and apply them to examples.

Core Idea
A weak opinion may be followed in necessity or by a mujtahid within the madhhab — but not by a layperson without excuse.

This passage refines a critical rasm al-mufti rule: the general principle is that weak (marjuh) opinions are not acted upon, but there are exceptions. Through the example of a wound that may break wudu, Ibn Abidin explains when necessity or ijtihad capacity permits following a weak opinion. Understanding these exceptions prevents both rigid inflexibility and arbitrary departure from the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State the baseline: normally, a mufti and layperson must follow the preponderant (rajih) opinion; weak (marjuh) opinions are not acted upon or given as fatwa.
This is the default to which the exceptions apply.
2
Analyze the first exception: necessity
Find in the passage the condition of 'darurah' (extreme hardship). Note that Ibn Abidin himself used a weak opinion when no valid prayer option existed otherwise, and then repeated his prayers afterward as caution.
Necessity is assessed strictly and may require later reparation.
3
Analyze the second exception: partial ijtihad
Identify the scenario where a mufti has ijtihad within the madhhab, even partial. He may weigh evidence and adopt a weak opinion if it appears stronger to him, making it rajih in his view.
This does not apply to laypersons (awamm).
4
Distinguish the mufti's role
Note that a mufti may also give fatwa on a weak opinion for a person in necessity, even if the mufti himself does not follow it permanently.
Ibn Nujaym and Ibn Abidin both support this.
5
Synthesize the refined rule
Combine the two exceptions: the blanket prohibition is lifted in necessity (for the affected person and for the mufti) or for the mujtahid within the madhhab. The layperson is still bound by the preponderant views except in necessity.
This balanced approach guards against both literalism and laxity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخرقةٍ بحيث لو تركه ،سال، فإنّه ناقض للوضوء. ولكن هناك قول ضعيف نقله صاحب الهداية بأنّ ذلك ليس بناقض، وهذا قول شاذ مرجوح. ولكن ذكر العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أنه يسوغ للمعذور تقليد هذا القول عند الضرورة، وأنه كان قد ابتلي مرةً بكي الحمصة ولم يجد ما تصح به صلاته على مذهب الحنفيّة بغير مشقة شديدة إلا على هذا القول. ويقول العلامة ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "فاضطررت إلى تقليد هذا القول، ثمّ لما عافانى الله تعالى منه أعدت صلوة تلك المدة." وكذلك ذكر ابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى في "البحر" أقوالاً ضعيفةً في بحث ألوان الدماء، ثم قال: "وفى معراج الدراية [?] مغزيّاً إلى فخر الأئمة: لو أفتى مفت بشيئ من هذه الأقوال في مواضع الضرورة طلباً للتيسير كان حسناً." وقال ابن عابدين بعد نقله: "وبه عُلم أنّ المُضطر له العمل بذلك لنفسه كما قلنا، وإن المفتى له الإفتاء به للمُضطر، فما مر من أنه ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به محمول على غير موضع الضرورة." وحاصل ما ذكره ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أن العمل بالمرجوح يحور في حالتين: الأولى: حالة الضرورة ورفع الحرج الشديد، والثانية: إذا كان المفتى من أهل الاجتهاد في المذهب، ولو كان اجتهاده جزئياً، فإنه يُرجح ما هو مرجوح في المذهب على أساس قوة دليله عنده، فيصير راجحاً حسب رأيه. وهذا معنى قول البيري في شرح الأشباه: "هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه؟ نعم! إذا كان له رأى." وما جاء في خزانة الروايات: "العالم الذي يعرف معنى النصوص والأخبار، وهو من أهل الدراية، يجوز له أن يعمل عليها، وإن كان مخالفاً لمذهبه." وكذا قال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في شرح عقود رسم المفتى ص 93 ثم قال: "وتقييده بذى الرأى أى المجتهد في المذهب مخرج للعامي كما قال فإنه يلزمه اتباع ما صححوا، لكن في غير موضع الضرورة كما علمته آنفا."
With a cloth such that if he left it, it would flow, then it is breaking of wudu. But there is a weak opinion transmitted by the author of al-Hidayah that it is not breaking, and this is an odd, weak opinion. However, Allamah Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned that it is permissible for a person with an excuse to follow this opinion in necessity, and that he himself was once afflicted with cautery of the chickpea and did not find a means by which his prayer would be valid according to the Hanafi school without severe hardship except by this opinion. And Allamah Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) says: 'So I was forced to follow this opinion, then when Allah cured me of it, I repeated the prayers of that period.' Similarly, Ibn Nujaym (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in al-Bahr weak opinions in the discussion of colors of blood, then said: 'In Miraj al-Dirayah, referring to Fakhr al-A'imma: If a mufti gives a fatwa concerning something from these opinions in places of necessity seeking ease, it would be good.' And Ibn Abidin said after quoting him: 'And through it, it is known that the one in necessity may act on that for himself as we said, and that the mufti may give fatwa on it for the one in necessity. So what has preceded—that he is not to act on the weak nor give fatwa on it—is applied to other than a place of necessity.' And the summary of what Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned is that acting on the weak opinion occurs in two cases: the first: the case of necessity and lifting severe hardship; the second: if the mufti is of those with ijtihad in the madhhab, even if his ijtihad is partial, for he preponderates what is weak in the madhhab based on the strength of its evidence in his view, so it becomes preponderant according to his opinion. This is the meaning of the statement of al-Biri in Sharh al-Ashbah: 'Is it permissible for a person to act on a weak narration in his own right? Yes! If he has an opinion.' And what is mentioned in Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'The scholar who knows the meaning of texts and reports, and is one of the people of insight, it is permissible for him to act upon them, even if they contradict his madhhab.' And thus Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) said in Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti, p.93, then said: 'And its restriction to one with opinion, i.e., the mujtahid in the madhhab, excludes the layperson as he said, for he must follow what they have deemed correct, but in other than a place of necessity as you have learned earlier.'
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage from the 'Summary of the Rules of Rasm al-Mufti' addresses a critical rasm rule: when is it permissible for a mufti or a layperson to act upon or give fatwa based on a weak (مرجوح) opinion within the Hanafi madhhab. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, demonstrates the rule through the example of the 'ki al-hammasa' treatment (cautery with a chickpea), where the prevailing view is that any moisture that would flow if left breaks wudu, but a weak opinion says it does not. Ibn Abidin notes that a person with a valid excuse may follow this weak opinion under necessity—he himself did so when no other option allowed his prayer to be valid. Ibn Nujaym supports this, citing the principle that a mufti may use weak opinions in situations of necessity seeking ease. Ibn Abidin then synthesizes the rule into two scenarios: (1) genuine necessity (ضرورة) where avoiding severe hardship (رفع الحرج الشديد) justifies following the weak opinion—here both the affected person and the mufti may act; (2) when the mufti is a mujtahid within the madhhab (أهل الاجتهاد في المذهب), even partial, who can weigh evidence and find the weak opinion stronger in his view—for him it becomes preponderant (راجح). This does not apply to a layperson (عامي), who must follow the relied-upon stance (ما صححوا) except in necessity. The passage thus refines the blanket prohibition of weak opinions by carving out these exceptions, guarding against both rigid literalism and reckless departure from the madhhab.

Key Terms
المرجوح (al-marjūḥ): A legal opinion within the Hanafi madhhab that is outweighed or weak relative to the preponderant (راجح) opinion; not to be followed without justification.
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): A situation of extreme necessity that would cause severe hardship or impossibility if the preponderant opinion were followed, making the weak opinion permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Abidin's summary, in which two scenarios is it permissible to act upon a weak (مرجوح) opinion in the Hanafi madhhab?
A) Necessity and when the mufti is a mujtahid within the madhhab
B) For any layperson who finds it easy and for a mufti who has no other opinion
C) Only when the weak opinion is from a later scholar and for all Muslims
D) Only in matters of worship (ibadat) and not in transactions (mu'amalat)

Key Takeaway
The blanket prohibition on weak opinions has two exceptions: necessity (for both mufti and layperson) and partial ijtihad within the madhhab (for the qualified scholar).

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

8 min
Permissibility of Acting on the Weak Opinion in the Hanafi Madhhab
Explains when a mufti may act upon or give fatwa with a weak opinion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two conditions under which a Hanafi mufti may act upon or issue a fatwa with a weak opinion (marjuh).

Core Idea
Acting on the weak opinion is permitted only in necessity or if the mufti has ijtihad.

In the Hanafi tradition, the relied-upon (rajih) opinions are the standard for fatwa and practice. However, the rasm al-mufti recognizes that rigid adherence to the preferred view may cause hardship in certain situations. This passage, drawing on Ibn Abidin and earlier authorities, outlines when a mufti may legitimately depart from the rajih and act on a weaker view. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for muftis to balance scholarly authority with practical ease.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Note the initial statement that the prohibition of acting on the weak (and giving fatwa with it) applies in normal circumstances.
2
Extract the first exception: necessity
Ibn Abidin explicitly permits acting on the weak in places of necessity (darura) to remove severe hardship (raf' al-haraj al-shadid). This applies both to the mufti's personal practice and giving fatwa for the one in need.
3
Extract the second exception: ijtihad in the madhhab
If the mufti is capable of ijtihad within the madhhab (even partial), he may weigh evidence and prefer a weak opinion if he finds its proof stronger. Thus the marjuh becomes rajih according to his own determination.
This ijtihad does not require full independence; partial ability suffices.
4
Apply the restrictions to laymen
The permission is restricted to scholars with ijtihad. A layman must follow the validated (sahhahu) opinions of the madhhab, except in necessity, where he too may follow a weak opinion for ease.
This clarifies the distinction between scholar and non-scholar.

Source Text

مفت بشيئ من هذه الأقوال في مواضع الضرورة طلباً للتيسير كان حسناً. وقال ابن عابدين بعد نقله: "وبه عُلم أنّ المُضطر له العمل بذلك لنفسه كما قلنا، وإن المفتى له الإفتاء به للمُضطر، فما مر من أنه ليس له العمل بالضعيف ولا الإفتاء به محمول على غير موضع الضرورة." وحاصل ماذكره ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى أن العمل بالمرجوح يحور في حالتين: الأولى: حالة الضرورة ورفع الحرج الشديد، والثانية: إذاكان المفتى من أهل الاجتهاد في المذهب، ولوكان اجتهاده جزئيّاً، فإنّه يُرجح ما هو مرجوح في المذهب على أساس قوة دليله عنده، فيصير راجحاً حسب رأيه. وهذا معنى قول البيري في شرح الأشباه: "هل يجوز للإنسان العمل بالضعيف من الرواية في حق نفسه ؟ نعم ! إذا كان له رأى " وماجاء في خزانة الروايات: "العالم الذى يعرف معنى النّصوص والأخبار، وهو من أهل الدراية، يجوز له أن يعمل عليها، وإن كان مخالفاً لمذهبه." وتقييده بذى الرأى أى المجتهد في المذهب مُخرج للعامي كما قال فإنّه يلزمه اتباع ما صححوا، لكن في غير موضع الضرورة كما علمته آنفا.
If one gives a fatwa with some of these statements in places of necessity seeking ease, it is good. Ibn Abidin said after quoting: 'It is known that the one in need may act on it for himself as we said, and the mufti may give fatwa with it for the one in need; what was mentioned earlier—that he may not act on the weak nor give fatwa with it—is restricted to other than situations of necessity.' The summary of what Ibn Abidin mentioned is that acting on the weak occurs in two situations: first, necessity and removal of severe hardship; second, if the mufti is one of those capable of ijtihad within the madhhab, even partial, then he gives weight to what is weak in the madhhab based on the strength of its evidence according to him, so it becomes strong according to his view. This is the meaning of al-Bayri's statement in his commentary on al-Ashbah: 'Is it permissible for a person to act on a weak narration concerning himself? Yes, if he has an opinion.' And what is mentioned in Khizanat al-Riwayat: 'A scholar who understands the meaning of texts and reports and is capable of discernment may act on them even if they contradict his madhhab.' And its restriction to one with an opinion, i.e., a mujtahid in the madhhab, excludes the layman, as he said; indeed, the layman must follow what they have validated, but in other than situations of necessity, as you learned earlier.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage addresses the rasm al-mufti rule regarding when it is permissible to act upon or give fatwa with a weak opinion (marjuh) in the Hanafi madhhab. The author first quotes a general principle that giving fatwa with various statements in necessity is acceptable. Then he attributes to Ibn Abidin the clarification that the prohibition of acting on weak narrations is only for normal circumstances. Two exceptions are identified: (1) necessity (darura) to remove severe hardship, and (2) when the mufti has ijtihad within the madhhab, even if partial, and he finds a strong evidence for the weak view. This echoes statements by al-Bayri and a text from Khizanat al-Riwayat. The final sentence from Ibn Abidin restricts the permission to those with independent reasoning (ahl al-ra'y), excluding the layman, unless in necessity. The authority of these rulings is from the later Hanafi tradition (Fatawa/Mutakhkhirin), not from the founding imams.

Key Terms
مرجوح (marjuh): The weaker opinion in the madhhab, not the relied-upon (rajih) view
ضرورة (darura): A situation of dire need that permits deviation from the standard ruling
اجتهاد في المذهب (ijtihad fi al-madhhab): Ability to derive rulings within the Hanafi school by weighing evidence, even if partial

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) There is a situation of necessity (darura) that requires ease.
C) The weak opinion must be from a later Hanafi authority.
D) The person acting on it is a scholar (not a layman), except in necessity.

Key Takeaway
Acting on a weak opinion is permissible in two specific circumstances: necessity and when the mufti possesses ijtihad (even partial) in the madhhab.

Fatwa According to Another Madhhab: Principle and First Exception
Sets the rule and first exception for mufti adopting another madhhab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first condition under which a Hanafi mufti may adopt the ruling of another madhhab and apply it to a scenario involving genuine hardship.

Core Idea
A mufti may adopt another madhhab only when his own madhhab imposes unbearable hardship — never out of personal preference.

In this passage, the author establishes the foundational rule that a mufti bound by taqlid must remain within his madhhab. However, he then provides a crucial refinement: this rule is not absolute. He explains the rationale behind taqlid — blocking means to caprice — and then details the first of three situations where following another madhhab is permissible: necessity or severe hardship. This lesson unpacks that principle and its first application.

Guided Path
1
State the base rule
What is the default obligation for a muqallid mufti? From the passage: he should not give fatwa except according to the madhhab of his imam.
This is established in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti.
2
Understand the rationale for taqlid
Why is a mufti restricted to one madhhab? The author explains that it is based on blocking the means (sadd al-dharā'i') and sharī' interests, to prevent people from following their desires.
This reframes taqlid as a protective measure, not an inherent limitation.
3
Recognize the universal validity of all madhhabs
The author affirms that all madhhabs are valid interpretations of the same Sharī'ah; no madhhab can be dismissed. The Sharī'ah encompasses all of them.
This is the basis for allowing adoption of another madhhab in cases of need.
4
Identify the first exception
When is it allowed to adopt another madhhab? In case of severe hardship (ḥaraj) or a real need (ḥājah) in one's own madhhab regarding a specific issue.
The condition is that the hardship must be unbearable (lā yuṭāq) or the need unavoidable (lā maḥīṣa ʿanhā).
5
Apply the condition
The exception requires that the adoption be for genuine need, not caprice (hawā). The mufti must have a valid sharī' reason to alleviate hardship.
Picking concessions based on desire is explicitly prohibited.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافتاء بمذهب آخر
الأصل للمفتى المقلّد أن لا يُفتي إلا بمذهب إمامه حسب القواعد التي ذكرناها عن "عقود رسم المفتى". ولكن الذى يجب أن لا يُغْفَلَ عنه ما فصلنا في مبحث التقليد والتمذهب من أنّ تقليد إمام معين فتوى مبنية على سد الذرائع والمصالح الشرعيّة، لئلا يقعَ النَّاسُ فى اتباع الهوى، فإن التقاط رُخص المذاهب بالهوى والتشهى حرام وإلا فالمحقق أن جميع مذاهب المجتهدين تفسيرات للشريعة نفسيها، لا سبيل للطعن في أحدٍ منها، لأن كل مجتهد بذل ما في وسعه من جهدٍ في الوصول إلى مُراد النصوص، واستخراج الأحكام منها فليست الشريعة منحصرةً فى مذهب إمام واحد، بل كل مذهب جزء من أجزاء الشريعة، وطريقة من طرق العمل بها. وإنما الشرع المنزل دائر بين سائر المذاهب، ومَن ظن أن الشريعة منحصرةٌ في مذهب واحد من هذه المذاهب، فإنّه مُخطئ بيقين. ومن هذه الجهة ربما يجوز لمفتى مذهب واحدٍ أن يختار قول المذهب الآخر للعمل أو الفتوى، بشرط أن لا يكونَ ذلك بالتشهى واتباع الهوى وإنّما يجوز ذلك في ثلاث حالات نذكرها بشيئ من التفصيل فيمايلي، ونسأل الله سبحانه التوفيق للسداد والصواب.
.١ الإفتاء بمذهب آخر لحاجة عامة
الحالة الأولى: الضرورة أو الحاجة وذلك أن يكون في المذهب في مسألة مخصوصة حرج شديد لا يُطاق، أو حاجة واقعية لا محيص عنها، فيجوز أن يُعمل بمذهب آخر دفعاً للحرج وإنجازاً للحاجة، وهذا كما أفتى علماء
Fatwa According to Another Madhhab
The principle for the muqallid mufti is that he should not give fatwa except according to the madhhab of his imam, according to the rules we have mentioned from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. But what must not be overlooked is what we detailed in the chapter on taqlīd and tamadhhub: that following a specific imam in fatwa is based on blocking the means (sadd al-dharā'i') and shar‘ī interests, so that people do not fall into following their desires. Indeed, picking and choosing the concessions (rukhas) of the madhhabs based on desire and caprice is prohibited. Otherwise, the verified position is that all madhhabs of the mujtahids are interpretations of the same Sharī‘ah; there is no way to object to any of them, because every mujtahid exerted his utmost effort in reaching the intended meaning of the texts and deriving rulings from them. The Sharī‘ah is not confined to a single imam's madhhab; rather, every madhhab is a part of the Sharī‘ah and a method of acting upon it. The revealed law encompasses all madhhabs, and whoever thinks that the Sharī‘ah is confined to one madhhab is definitely mistaken. From this perspective, it is sometimes permissible for a mufti of a single madhhab to choose the opinion of another madhhab for action or fatwa, provided it is not due to caprice and following desire. Rather, it is permissible in three situations, which we will detail below. We ask Allah for success and correctness.
1. Fatwa According to Another Madhhab for a General Need
The first situation: necessity or need. That is, when in the madhhab, regarding a specific issue, there is severe unbearable hardship, or a real necessity that cannot be avoided. In that case, it is permissible to act according to another madhhab to remove the hardship and fulfill the need. This is as the scholars have given fatwa...
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning when a mufti who follows a specific madhhab may issue a fatwa according to another madhhab. The author first states the general principle: a muqallid mufti must only give fatwa according to his own imam's madhhab, as established in 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. However, he emphasizes an important nuance: the entire system of taqlīd is built upon the principles of sadd al-dharā'i' (blocking the means to evil) and masālih shar'iyyah (shar‘ī interests) to prevent people from following their desires. Picking and choosing concessions from various madhhabs based on whims is haram. Nevertheless, all madhhabs are valid interpretations of the same Sharia; no madhhab can be dismissed. The Sharia encompasses all of them. This allows a mufti, under specific conditions, to adopt a ruling from another madhhab. The key condition: it must not be for caprice or desire. The author then lists three situations (only the first is given in this passage). The first situation is 'necessary or need': if within his own madhhab there is an unbearable hardship or an unavoidable real need in a particular issue, it is then permissible to take the ruling of another madhhab to alleviate hardship. The text begins an example of scholars doing so, but it is cut off.

Key Terms
التقليد (al-taqlīd): Following a specific imam's madhhab in fatwa and practice, which is based on sadd al-dharā'i' and maṣāliḥ shar‘iyyah.
التمذهب (al-tamadhhub): Adhering to a particular madhhab as one's method of practicing the Sharia.
رخص المذاهب (rukhas al-madhāhib): The concessions or lenient rulings from various madhhabs; picking them based on desire is prohibited.
سد الذرائع (sadd al-dharā'i‘): Blocking the means that could lead to evil; here used as justification for restricting a mufti to one madhhab.
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Severe hardship or constraint that makes following one's own madhhab unbearable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it permissible for a Hanafi mufti to give a fatwa according to the Shafi'i madhhab?
A) Whenever he finds the Shafi'i ruling easier.
B) When there is severe hardship or a real need in the Hanafi madhhab regarding a specific issue.
C) If he prefers the Shafi'i evidence over Hanafi evidence.
D) Only if he is a mujtahid himself.

Key Takeaway
A mufti may temporarily adopt another madhhab's ruling only to remove genuine hardship, not out of personal convenience.

Historical Precedents for Hanafi Fatwa from Other Madhhabs
Examples of Hanafi fatwa according to other madhhabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify three historical examples where Hanafi scholars gave fatwa according to another madhhab and explain the rationale of need or widespread affliction.

Core Idea
Hanafi muftis can adopt another madhhab's ruling when genuine widespread hardship arises.

This lesson explores how later Hanafi scholars, faced with real-world difficulties, turned to Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali rulings to ease hardship. We will examine specific cases such as seizing any property from a debtor (zafar) and the option of the defrauded buyer (khiyar al-maghbun).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its original Hanafi position
For each example, state the default Hanafi ruling that was being set aside.
E.g., the Hanafi view on zafar: creditor can only take property of the same genus as the debt.
2
Understand the problem (need/widespread affliction)
Determine why the default ruling became impractical or caused hardship.
E.g., people persisted in obstructing payment, making it difficult to collect debts.
3
Note the adopted madhhab and its ruling
Identify which other school's view was adopted and how it differed.
E.g., Shafi'i allows taking any property, regardless of genus.
4
Trace the authority
Which later Hanafi scholar endorsed this practice? Cite the reference.
E.g., Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar, Ibn Nujaym in Sharh al-Ashbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافتاء بمذهب آخر
الحنفيّة بمذهب الشافعيّة في جواز الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن، وبمذهب المالكية في مسألة زوجة المفقود والعنين والمتعنت. وكذلك يدخل في هذا النوع ما عمّ فيه البلوي. و مثاله أنّ المتأخرين من علماء الحنفية قد أفتوا بمذهب الشافعي في مسألة الظفر ) في أنه يجوز للظافر أخذ حقه من أي مال كان سواء كان من جنس الواجب أو من خلاف جنسه، وذلك لتغير الناس في مداومة العقوق صرح به ابن عابدين في كتاب الحجر . وكذلك أفتى المتأخرون من الحنفية بمذهب مالك رحمه الله تعالى في مسألة خيار المغبون فى أنه يجوز ردّ المبيع بغبن فاحش إذا كان فيه غرور، صرح به ابن عابدين في رد المحتار تحت باب المرابحة والتولية ) وابن نجيم رحمه الله تعالى في شرح الأشباه والنظائر تحت قاعدة "المشقة تَجْلِبُ التيسيير" وكذلك أفتى الفقهاء الحنفية بمذهب الشافعيّة بضمان منافع المغصوب في مال اليتيم، ومال الوقف، وما أعد للاستغلال. بل اقترح ابن أمير حاج رحمه الله تعالى أن يُفتى بضمان المنافع بالغصب مطلقاً.
وقد تعقدت في عصرنا المعاملات، وكثرت فيها حاجات الناس، ولا سيما بعد حدوث الصناعات الكبيرة وشيوع التجارة فيما بين البلدان والأقاليم، فينبغى للمفتى أن يُسهل على النّاس في الأخذ بما هو أرفق فيما تعم به البلوى سواء كان فى غير مذهبه من المذاهب الأربعة، وقد أوصى بذلك شيخ مشايخنا العلامة رشيد أحمد الكنكوهي رحمه الله تعالى صاحبه الشيخ العلامة أشرف علي التهانوي رحمه الله تعالي، وقد عمل بذلك الشيخ التهانوي قدس الله سره فى كثير من المسائل في "إمداد الفتاوى"، فأفتى بقول الشافعية في عدم اشتراط وجود المسلم فيه إلى حلول الأجل، وجواز السلم الحال، وبمذهب المالكية في جواز الشركة بالعروض، وبمذهب الحنابلة في جواز المضاربة فى منافع الدابّة. ولكن يجب لجواز الافتاء بمذهب آخر بسبب الحاجة أو عموم البلوى أن تتحقق شروط آتية:
الأول: أن تكون الحاجة شديدة، والبلوى عامة فى نفس الأمر لا مجرد الوهم بذلك.
الثاني: أن يتأكد المفتى بمسيس الحاجة، وذلك بمشاورة غيره من أصحاب الفتوى وأصحاب الخبرة فى ذلك المجال والأحسن أن لا يتبادر بالإفتاء منفرداً عن غيره، بل يُحاوِلُ بالقدر المستطاع أن يضم معه فتوى غيره من العلماء، وخاصةً إذا أراد أن ينشر الفتوى على نطاق واسع.
Giving fatwa according to another madhhab: The Hanafis [gave fatwa] according to the Shafi'i madhhab regarding the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran, and according to the Maliki madhhab in the issue of the wife of the missing person, the impotent, and the one who refrains from intercourse. Also included in this type is what is widespread (ma 'amma fihi al-balwa). An example is that later Hanafi scholars gave fatwa according to the Shafi'i madhhab in the issue of al-zafar (taking one's right from any property of the debtor), that it is permissible for the one who seizes to take his right from any property, whether it is of the same type as the debt or not, because people had changed in persisting in obstinacy. Ibn Abidin stated this in the chapter on interdiction. Similarly, later Hanafis gave fatwa according to the Maliki madhhab in the issue of khiyar al-maghbun (option of the defrauded), that it is permissible to return the sold item due to gross fraud if there is deception. Ibn Abidin stated this in Radd al-Muhtar under the chapter on murabahah and tawliyah, and Ibn Nujaym in Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir under the maxim "Hardship brings ease." Likewise, Hanafi jurists gave fatwa according to the Shafi'i madhhab regarding liability for the usufruct of usurped property in the wealth of an orphan, endowment property, and property intended for leasing. Ibn Amir Hajj even suggested that fatwa be given on absolute liability for usufruct by usurpation. Transactions have become complicated in our time, and people's needs have increased, especially after the emergence of large industries and widespread trade between countries and regions. Therefore, the mufti should make things easy for people by adopting what is more convenient in matters of general affliction, even if it is from outside his own madhhab among the four schools. Our teacher's teacher, Allamah Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi, recommended this to his companion, Allamah Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, and al-Tahanawi acted upon it in many issues in Imdad al-Fatawa. He gave fatwa according to the Shafi'i view on the non-requirement of the existence of the subject matter until the due date in salam, and the permissibility of spot salam; according to the Maliki madhhab on the permissibility of partnership with commodities; and according to the Hanbali madhhab on the permissibility of mudarabah in the services of an animal. However, for the permissibility of giving fatwa according to another madhhab due to need or general affliction, the following conditions must be verified: First: The need must be severe and the affliction must be general in reality, not just imagined. Second: The mufti must be certain of the pressing need, by consulting other fatwa-givers and experts in that field. It is better that he does not rush to give fatwa alone, but rather tries as much as possible to include the fatwa of other scholars, especially if he wants to publish the fatwa on a wide scale.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage discusses a critical principle in the Hanafi fatwa methodology: when necessity or widespread affliction arises, a Hanafi mufti may depart from his own madhhab and issue a fatwa based on another recognized madhhab (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali). The passage begins by providing examples from Hanafi juristic practice. For instance, some later Hanafis followed the Shafi'i view on hiring for Quran teaching, and the Maliki view on the wife of a missing or impotent husband. The key example is the issue of "zafar" (seizing property): the original Hanafi position restricts the creditor to taking only property of the same genus as the debt, but due to widespread obstruction (people persisting in delaying payment), later scholars adopted the Shafi'i position allowing seizure of any property. Similarly, in cases of fraud (ghabn fahish), the Hanafi view is that there is no option to return the item, but following the Maliki view, they permitted return if there is deception, citing the maxim "hardship brings ease" (al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir). Another example is liability for usufruct of usurped property, where the Hanafi school does not normally impose liability on the usurper for the benefit taken, but due to the prevalence of endowments and orphan property, they adopted the Shafi'i view imposing liability. Ibn Amir Hajj even suggested this be extended universally. The passage then moves to contemporary application, noting that transactions have become complex with large industries and international trade. The mufti should facilitate for people by adopting the more convenient ruling from any of the four madhhabs in matters of general affliction. This was recommended by Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi to Ashraf Ali al-Tahanawi, who implemented it in his fatawa collection Imdad al-Fatawa, giving fatwas according to Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali views on specific issues. Finally, the passage lays down two essential conditions for this practice: (1) the need must be real and severe, and the affliction genuinely widespread – not merely imagined; (2) the mufti must verify the urgency by consulting other qualified scholars and experts. He should not act alone, especially when publishing the fatwa widely. This principle underscores the flexibility within the Hanafi tradition to address changing circumstances while maintaining methodological discipline.

Key Terms
الافتاء بمذهب آخر (al-ifta' bi-madhhab akhar): Issuing a legal ruling based on a school of law other than one's own (Hanafi) due to need or widespread affliction.
عموم البلوى (umum al-balwa): A situation where a particular issue becomes widespread among people, making it difficult to adhere to the original ruling.
الحاجة (al-hajah): Necessity or pressing need that requires a relaxation of the normal ruling.
الظفر (al-zafar): Seizing property of a debtor by the creditor without the debtor's consent, typically limited to property of the same genus in Hanafi fiqh.
خيار المغبون (khiyar al-maghbun): The option of the defrauded buyer to rescind a sale due to gross fraud (ghabn fahish).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did later Hanafi scholars adopt the Shafi'i ruling on zafar (seizing property)?
A) Because the Shafi'i ruling is more logical.
B) Because people had changed and persisted in obstructing payment.
C) Because the Hanafi ruling was based on a weak hadith.
D) Because the Shafi'i ruling was easier for the rich.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi muftis have a historical precedent for adopting another madhhab's ruling when widespread affliction creates genuine hardship.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
The Two Conditions for Issuing Fatwa from Another Madhhab
Conditions for Hanafi mufti to use another madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply the two conditions for a Hanafi mufti to issue a fatwa according to another madhhab: severe genuine need and consultation with other scholars.

Core Idea
Issuing fatwa from another madhhab requires rigorous verification of widespread affliction and scholarly consensus.

This lesson details the safeguards put in place by Hanafi authorities to prevent arbitrary picking of madhhabs. The mufti must ensure the need is real and must not act alone, especially when the fatwa is to be published widely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
What is the first requirement mentioned? Explain the difference between real and imagined widespread affliction.
The passage states: 'the need must be severe and the affliction must be general in reality, not merely imagined.'
2
Understand 'real vs. imagined'
Why is this distinction important? Consider the danger of relying on subjective perception.
A mufti must confirm the affliction is actually widespread, not just based on a few complaints.
3
Identify the second condition
What is the second requirement? Why must the mufti consult others?
The mufti must be certain of the need by consulting other fatwa-givers and experts, and should not rush to issue a fatwa alone.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a modern case, evaluate whether the conditions are met. For example, widespread need for spot salam in a Muslim country.
Check: Is the need severe? Is it genuinely widespread? Has the mufti consulted other scholars?

مشاورة (mushawarah): Consultation with other scholars and experts to verify the pressing need.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the second condition for issuing fatwa according to another madhhab?
A) The mufti must be an expert in the other madhhab.
B) The mufti must consult other fatwa-givers and experts.
C) The fatwa must be approved by a committee of scholars from all four madhhabs.
D) The mufti must have a fatwa from the other madhhab's mufti.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi mufti may issue fatwa from another madhhab only when the need is genuinely widespread and severe, and after consulting other scholars.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Conditions for Issuing Fatwa by Another Madhhab
Lists four conditions for justified use of non-Hanafi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions for issuing a fatwa by another madhhab and apply them to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Cross-madhhab fatwa is permissible only under four strict conditions, not as a mere convenience.

This lesson examines when and how a mufti may issue a fatwa based on a school other than his own. The Hanafi tradition permits this only under pressing circumstances, but with firm safeguards. We will learn the four essential conditions and their rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The need must be severe (hajat shadidah) and the exigency widespread (balwa 'ammah) in reality, not imagined. This prevents frivolous switching.
The mufti must verify reality, not just assume.
2
Identify the second condition
The mufti must be certain of the need by consulting other muftis and experts. He should not act alone, especially when issuing public fatwas.
Consultation ensures objectivity and prevents individual bias.
3
Identify the third condition
The mufti must thoroughly research the other madhhab's position by consulting its scholars and understanding its terminology. Reading one or two books is insufficient.
Each madhhab has its own terminology and methods.
4
Identify the fourth condition
The adopted view must not be a deviant opinion (shadhdh) that contradicts the majority of jurists. The hadith about the ummah not uniting on error is cited.
Avoiding tatarruq al-rukhas is essential.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تعقدت في عصرنا المعاملات، وكثرت فيها حاجات الناس، ولا سيما بعد حدوث الصناعات الكبيرة وشيوع التجارة فيما بين البلدان والأقاليم، فينبغى للمفتى أن يُسهل على النّاس في الأخذ بما هو أرفق فيما تعم به البلوى سواء كان فى غير مذهبه من المذاهب الأربعة، وقد أوصى بذلك شيخ مشايخنا العلامة رشيد أحمد الكنكوهي رحمه الله تعالى صاحبه الشيخ العلامة أشرف علي التهانوي رحمه الله تعالي، وقد عمل بذلك الشيخ التهانوي قدس الله سره فى كثير من المسائل في "إمداد الفتاوى"، فأفتى بقول الشافعية في عدم اشتراط وجود المسلم فيه إلى حلول الأجل، وجواز السلم الحال، وبمذهب المالكية في جواز الشركة بالعروض، وبمذهب الحنابلة في جواز المضاربة فى منافع الدابّة. ولكن يجب لجواز الافتاء بمذهب آخر بسبب الحاجة أو عموم البلوى أن تتحقق شروط آتية:
الأول: أن تكون الحاجة شديدة، والبلوى عامة فى نفس الأمر لا مجرد الوهم بذلك.
الثاني: أن يتأكد المفتى بمسيس الحاجة، وذلك بمشاورة غيره من أصحاب الفتوى وأصحاب الخبرة فى ذلك المجال والأحسن أن لا يتبادر بالإفتاء منفرداً عن غيره، بل يُحاوِلُ بالقدر المستطاع أن يضم معه فتوى غيره من العلماء، وخاصةً إذا أراد أن ينشر الفتوى على نطاق واسع.
الثالث: أن يتأكد و يتثبت في تحقيق المذهب الذى يُريد أن يُفتي به تحقيقاً بالغاً، والأحسن أن يُراجع فى ذلك علماء ذلك المذهب، ولا يكتفى برؤية مسألة في كتاب أو كتابين، لأن كل مذهب له مصطلحات تخصه، وأساليب ينفرد بها، وربّما لا يصل إلى مُرادها الحقيقي إلا من مارس هذه المصطلحات والأساليب.
الرابع: أن لا يكون القول المأخوذ به من الأقوال الشاذة التي تُخالف جماهير فقهاء الأمة، ووقع منهم الإنكار عليها. روى عبدالله بن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنهما عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إِنَّ اللَّهَ لَا يَجْمَعُ أُمَّتِي أَوْقَالَ: أُمَّةَ مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَلَى ضَلَالَةٍ، وَيَدَ اللَّهِ عَلَى الْجَمَاعَةِ، وَمَنْ شَدَّ شَدَّ إِلَى النَّارِ. وروى عن أنس بن مالك رضى الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: "إِنَّ أُمَّتِي لا تَجْتَمِعُ عَلَى صَلَالَةٍ، فَإِذَا رَأَيْتُمْ اخْتِلَافًا، فَعَلَيْكُمْ بِالسَّوَادِ الأَعْظم" وقد صدرت من بعض الفقهاء تفردات لم يأخذ بها جماهير أهل العلم، بل وقع منهم الإنكار عليها. وإن اللجوء إلى تلك التفردات طلباً للتيسير وتتبعاً للرخص مما شنّع عليه السلف قديماً وحديثاً.
Transactions have become complicated in our time, and people's needs have increased therein, especially after the emergence of large industries and the prevalence of trade between countries and regions. So the mufti should make it easy for people to adopt what is more convenient in matters of widespread exigency, whether it is in other than his own madhhab from the four madhhabs. The teacher of our teachers, Allamah Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi (may Allah have mercy on him) advised that to his companion Sheikh Allamah Ashraf Ali al-Thanwi (may Allah have mercy on him), and Sheikh al-Thanwi (may Allah sanctify his secret) acted upon that in many issues in "Imdad al-Fatawa", so he gave fatwa according to the Shafi'i view regarding the non-requirement of the existence of the subject matter of salam until the term, and the permissibility of immediate salam; according to the Maliki view regarding the permissibility of partnership with goods; and according to the Hanbali view regarding the permissibility of mudarabah in the usufruct of an animal. However, for the permissibility of issuing fatwa by another madhhab due to need or widespread exigency, the following conditions must be realized: (1) First: that the need be severe and the exigency widespread in reality, not merely imaginary. (2) Second: that the mufti be certain of the pressing need, by consulting other fatwa givers and experts in that field; and it is better that he not proceed to give fatwa alone without others, rather he should strive as much as possible to include with him the fatwa of other scholars, especially if he wants to publish the fatwa widely. (3) Third: that he ascertain and thoroughly verify the madhhab he wants to give fatwa by, with full investigation; and it is better that he consult scholars of that madhhab in that matter, and not be satisfied with seeing an issue in one or two books, because each madhhab has its own terminology and unique methods, and perhaps one cannot reach its true intent except one who has practiced these terminologies and methods. (4) Fourth: that the view adopted should not be from the deviant opinions (shadhdhah) that contradict the majority of the jurists of the ummah, and from whom disapproval has occurred. 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) narrated from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) that he said: "Verily Allah does not unite my ummah – or he said: the ummah of Muhammad (peace be upon him) – on error, and the hand of Allah is with the jama'ah, and whoever deviates deviates to the Fire." And it was narrated from Anas ibn Malik (may Allah be pleased with him) from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: "My ummah does not unite on error, so when you see disagreement, then stick to the great majority." There have occurred from some jurists isolated opinions that the majority of scholars did not adopt, rather disapproval occurred from them. And resorting to those isolated opinions seeking ease and following licenses (tatarruq al-rukhas) is something the predecessors condemned, both past and present.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning when a Hanafi mufti may issue a fatwa based on another madhhab due to need or widespread exigency. The author, Mufti Muhammad Taqi Usmani, begins by noting the complexity of modern transactions and advises muftis to facilitate matters for people by adopting more convenient rulings from other madhhabs when hardship is widespread. He cites the example of his teacher's teacher, Rashid Ahmad al-Kankohi, who advised Ashraf Ali al-Thanwi, who himself acted on this in Imdad al-Fatawa—e.g., allowing salam without immediate delivery (Shafi'i), partnership with goods (Maliki), and mudarabah in animal usufruct (Hanbali). Then he presents four conditions that must be met for such cross-madhhab fatwa to be permissible. Condition 1: The need must be genuine and widespread, not imagined. Condition 2: The mufti must confirm the need by consulting other fatwa-givers and experts; he should not act alone, especially for wide publication. Condition 3: The mufti must thoroughly research the other madhhab's position by consulting its scholars and understanding its terminology, not merely reading one or two books. Condition 4: The adopted view must not be a deviant (shadhdh) opinion that contradicts the consensus of the majority of jurists. He supports this with hadiths about the ummah not uniting on error and the obligation to follow the majority (al-sawad al-a‘zam). He warns against 'tatarruq al-rukhas'—seeking out minority opinions merely to find ease—which the salaf condemned. This is a crucial principle for responsible fatwa-giving: while flexibility is allowed, it is tightly constrained to prevent abuse.

Key Terms
الإفتاء بمذهب آخر (al-ifta' bi-madhhab akhar): Giving a fatwa according to a school of law other than one's own due to need or widespread exigency.
الحاجة الشديدة (al-hajat al-shadidah): A genuine, pressing need that would cause hardship if not addressed, not mere desire.
البلوى العامة (al-balwa al-'ammah): A situation that affects a large number of people, making it difficult to adhere to the default ruling.
الأقوال الشاذة (al-aqwal al-shadhdhah): Isolated opinions that contradict the majority of reputable jurists and have been rejected by them.
تتبع الرخص (tatabbu' al-rukhas): The practice of seeking out the easiest opinions from different madhhabs without legitimate need, which is condemned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Mufti Taqi Usmani, what is the first condition for issuing a fatwa by another madhhab due to need?
A) The mufti must have studied that madhhab extensively.
B) The need must be severe and the exigency widespread in reality, not imaginary.
C) The opinion must be from a reliable book.
D) The mufti must obtain permission from a scholar of that madhhab.

Key Takeaway
Cross-madhhab fatwa is a concession permitted only under four strict conditions that prevent abuse and maintain the integrity of Islamic jurisprudence.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
The Prohibition of Following Every Dispensation (Rukhas al-Madhahib)
Warns against indiscriminate following of dispensations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prohibition of selectively following dispensations from different madhhabs and explain why it weakens one's religion.

Core Idea
Following every rukha from any madhhab without principle destroys one's faith.

Imams al-Awza'i, al-Dhahabi, Ahmad, and others warned that picking concessions from different schools leads to moral decay. This lesson examines their warnings and the principle that the mufti must follow the strongest evidence, not the easiest path.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being prohibited
What exactly is 'tattabu' al-rukhas'? It is the practice of selecting the easiest ruling from any school on each issue without consistency.
The warnings are directed at laypersons and muftis alike.
2
Recognize the authorities cited
Who said what? Note the strong language from al-Awza'i (leaving Islam), al-Dhahabi (weakened religion), and Ahmad (sinner).
These are reliable early scholars whose statements carry weight.
3
Understand the consequence
The consequence is described as 'gathering evil' and 'exposing oneself to dissolution.' This shows the severity.
The passage uses examples like mut'ah, nabidh, singing, and circumventing riba.
4
Contrast with the correct method
The correct method is to adopt the view that has the strongest evidence and is consistent with Sharia objectives and majority opinions.
This is the principle for muftis: take the rajih (preponderant) view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الأوزاعي رحمه الله تعالى: "من أخذ بنوادر العلماء خرج من الإسلام." وقال الحافظ الذهبي رحمه الله تعالى: "ومن تتبع رُخص المذاهب وزلات المجتهدين فقد رقّ دينه، كما قال الأوزاعي وغيره: من أخذ بقول المكيّين فى المُتعة، والكوفيين فى النبيذ، والمدنيين في الغناء، والشامتين في عصمة الخلفاء فقد جمع الشر. وكذا من أخذ في البيوع الربوية بمن يحتال عليها، وفي الطلاق ونكاح التحليل بمن توسع فيه، وشبه ذلك، فقد تعرض للانحلال." وقال الإمام أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله تعالى: "لو أن رجلاً عمل بِكُلِّ رُخصة : بقول أهل الكوفة في النبيذ، وأهل المدينة في السماع، وأهل مكة فى المتعة، كان فاسقاً." وقال معمر: "لو أن رجلاً أخذ بقول أهل المدينة في السماع يعنى الغناء، وإتيان النساء في أدبارهن، وبقولِ أهل مكة في المتعة والصرف، وبقول أهل الكوفة فى المُسْكر كان أشرّ عباد الله تعالى." وقال سليمانُ السَّيْمِي: "لو أخذت برخصة كل عالم أو قال: زلة كل عالم اجتمع فيك الشر كله." وقال عبدالرحمن بن مهدي رحمه الله تعالى: "لا يكون إماماً في العلم من أخذ بالشاذ، ولا إماماً في العلم من روى عن كل أحد، ولا يكون إماماً من حدث بكل ما سمع." هذا مارأوه في الأقوال الشاذة التي صدرت من الفقهاء الكبار الموثوقين الذين شهد لهم أهل العلم بالتفقه والورع، فما بالك بالأقوال الشاذة الصادرة من بعض من لاعلاقة له بالعلم والفقه وإنّما قال ماقال بناء على آراءه المتطرفة، أو عواطفه النفسية، أو على ثقافات أجنبية لا تمت إلى الإسلام بصلة. فيجب الأخذ بما هو أرجح دليلاً وأقوى حجة بالنظر إلى مصادر الشريعة الإسلامية ومقاصدها النبيلة وأقوال جماهير الفقهاء. الخامس: أن يؤخذ ذلك المذهب بجميع شروطه المعتبرة فيه، لئلا يؤدى ذلك إلى التلفيق فى مسألة واحدة. ومن المناسب أن نذكر هنا بعض التفصيل فى مسألة التلفيق، والله سبحانه ولي التوفيق.
حكم التلفيق
الذي تلخص لي فى موضوع التلفيق أن هذا الاصطلاح يُقصد به في عامة كلام الفقهاء أن يُختار مذهبان فى مسألةٍ واحدةٍ بحيث تحدث منه حالةٌ مركبة لا تجوز في أحد المذهبين مثل أن يأخذ المرأُ بقول الحنفية فى عدم انتقاض الوضوء بمَسَّ المرأة، وبمذهب الشافعية في عدمه بالدم السائل، ويُصلّى بعد ما مست امرأةً وسال منه دم، فإنّ هذه الصلوة لا تصح في أحدٍ من المذهبين. وقال القرافي رحمه الله تعالى: العلامة القرافي: هو أحمد بن أبي العلاء إدريس بن عبد الرحمن القرافي المصري، المالكي، أبو العباس شهاب الدين الإمام الأصولي الذي عدّه الإمام السيوطي من المجتهدين وإن كان منتسبا إلى مذهب الإمام مالك رحمهم الله تعالى، والقرافي نسبة إلى بقعة القرافة بمصر التي سكنها الإمام لمدة يسيرة. ولد رحمه الله سنة ٦٢٦ هـ. وأخذ العلم عن جهابذة علماء عصره كالإمام عزّ الدين بن عبد السلام والإمام ابن الحاجب، صاحب "الكافية" و "الشافية" وغيرهم رحهم الله تعالى. له تصانيف في غاية النفع، منها: "الإحكام في تمييز الفتاوى عن الأحكام"، و "أنوار البروق في أنواء الفروق"، و"الذخيرة" في فروع المالكية وغيرها. تُوفي رحمه الله سنة ٦٨٤ (ملخص من مقدمة التحقيق للفروق لفضيلة الشيخ عمر حسن القيام).
Imam al-Awza'i said: 'Whoever takes from the rare opinions of scholars leaves Islam.' Al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi said: 'Whoever follows the dispensations of the schools and the slips of the mujtahids has weakened his religion, as al-Awza'i and others said: Whoever takes the saying of the Meccans on mut'ah, the Kufans on nabidh, the Medinans on singing, and the Syrians on the infallibility of the caliphs has gathered evil. Similarly, whoever takes in ribawi sales from those who circumvent, and in divorce and analytic marriage from those who are lenient, and similar things, exposes himself to dissolution.' Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: 'If a man acted with every dispensation: the saying of the people of Kufa on nabidh, the people of Medina on listening, and the people of Mecca on mut'ah, he would be a sinner.' Ma'mar said: 'If a man took the saying of the people of Medina on listening (meaning singing) and coming to women from behind, and the saying of the people of Mecca on mut'ah and currency exchange, and the saying of the people of Kufa on intoxicants, he would be the worst of Allah's servants.' Sulayman al-Saymi said: 'If you take the dispensation of every scholar—or he said: the slip of every scholar—all evil would gather in you.' Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi said: 'He is not an imam in knowledge who takes from the shadhdh, nor an imam in knowledge who narrates from everyone, nor an imam who narrates everything he hears.' This is what they opined regarding the irregular opinions issued by great reliable jurists whom the people of knowledge attested to possess fiqh and piety. What then of the irregular opinions issued by those who have no connection to knowledge and fiqh, but only said what they said based on extremist views, or personal emotions, or foreign cultures that have no relation to Islam? So it is obligatory to take that which is stronger in evidence and more powerful in argument with reference to the sources of Islamic law, its noble objectives, and the statements of the majority of jurists. Fifth: That school is taken with all its valid conditions, so that this does not lead to talfiq in a single issue. It is appropriate to mention here some detail on the issue of talfiq, and Allah is the granter of success.
The Ruling on Talfiq
What has become clear to me on the topic of talfiq is that this term is generally used by jurists to mean that two schools are chosen in a single issue such that a composite situation arises that is not permissible in either of the two schools. For example, a person takes the Hanafi view that wudu is not broken by touching a woman, and the Shafi'i view that it is not broken by flowing blood, and then prays after touching a woman and blood flowed from him. This prayer is not valid in either school. And al-Qarafi said: (footnote: al-Allamah al-Qarafi is Ahmad ibn Abi al-Ala Idris ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Qarafi al-Misri al-Maliki...)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule prohibiting the practice of indiscriminately following dispensations and irregularities from different schools, and defines the concept of talfiq (patchwork) in fatwa. The author begins by quoting several early authorities warning that assembling dispensations from various madhhabs leads to moral and religious decay. Al-Awza'i states that taking from rare opinions amounts to leaving Islam. Al-Dhahabi and others warn that following every rukha (concession) and zalla (slip) of scholars weakens one's faith. The passage then cites Imam Ahmad and others to emphasize that such selective picking is tantamount to sinfulness and even the worst of deeds. The key point is that even if the source scholars are reliable, their irregular opinions (shadhdh) should not be followed; how much more so when those opinions come from unqualified persons. The author concludes that one must adopt the view that has the strongest evidence and is most consistent with the goals of sharia and the majority of jurists. Then, as a condition for following another madhhab (the fifth point), the author states that one must follow all the conditions of that madhhab to avoid talfiq in a single issue. He then defines talfiq: combining parts of rulings from different madhhabs in one issue such that the resulting composite act is not valid according to either school. The example given is a person who prays after touching a woman (Hanafi: does not invalidate wudu) and having flowing blood (Shafi'i: does not invalidate wudu); his prayer would be invalid in both madhhabs because the composite situation (touching woman + flowing blood) would break wudu in the Shafi'i school (due to touching) and in the Hanafi school (due to flowing blood, as blood invalidates wudu in Hanafi if it is flowing). The author then begins to cite al-Qarafi, but the passage cuts off. This lesson teaches that talfiq corrupts worship and is prohibited; the mufti and layman must avoid it.

Key Terms
اتباع الرخص (ittibā' al-rukhas): Following the dispensations or easy rulings from different madhhabs without consistency
شاذ (shādhdh): An irregular opinion opposed to the majority or stronger evidence
زلة العالم (zallat al-‘ālim): A slip or mistake of a scholar, an opinion that deviates from the stronger evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence of following every dispensation and slip of scholars?
A) It is permissible as long as each ruling is from a valid school.
B) It weakens one's religion and leads to dissolution.
C) It is only a minor sin that can be easily forgiven.
D) It makes one a great scholar due to knowledge of many schools.

Key Takeaway
The essential point: following every dispensation weakens religion; the mufti must adhere to strong evidence and avoid talfiq.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Ruling on Talfiq: Combining Madhhabs Invalidly
Defines talfiq and provides an example of invalidity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define talfiq, identify an example, and state the ruling that such composite acts are invalid.

Core Idea
Talfiq: combining rulings from two madhhabs in one act such that it is invalid in both.

After warning against following dispensations, the author defines the critical concept of talfiq—when a person mixes rulings from different schools in a single matter, creating a composite that is not valid in any school. This lesson dissects the definition and example.

Guided Path
1
Define talfiq literally and technically
The term talfiq linguistically means 'patchwork.' Technically, it is combining rulings from two madhhabs in one issue such that the resulting act is not valid in either school.
The key condition is that the composite act must be invalid in both schools.
2
Identify the example from the text
The example: a person takes Hanafi view that touching woman does not break wudu, and Shafi'i view that flowing blood does not break wudu. He then prays after touching a woman and having blood flow. His prayer is invalid in both schools.
In Hanafi, blood invalidates wudu; in Shafi'i, touching woman invalidates wudu. So the composite state (touch + blood) leaves him without valid wudu in either school.
3
Understand why it is prohibited
Talfiq is prohibited because it leads to an act that is not recognized by any valid school, thus it lacks legal validity.
The earlier warnings about following rukhas reinforce this prohibition.
4
Note the condition for following another madhhab
The author's fifth point: if one follows another madhhab, he must take it with all its conditions to avoid talfiq.
This means consistency: you cannot pick and choose within a single issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام الأوزاعي رحمه الله تعالى: "من أخذ بنوادر العلماء خرج من الإسلام." وقال الحافظ الذهبي رحمه الله تعالى: "ومن تتبع رُخص المذاهب وزلات المجتهدين فقد رقّ دينه، كما قال الأوزاعي وغيره: من أخذ بقول المكيّين فى المُتعة، والكوفيين فى النبيذ، والمدنيين في الغناء، والشامتين في عصمة الخلفاء فقد جمع الشر. وكذا من أخذ في البيوع الربوية بمن يحتال عليها، وفي الطلاق ونكاح التحليل بمن توسع فيه، وشبه ذلك، فقد تعرض للانحلال." وقال الإمام أحمد بن حنبل رحمه الله تعالى: "لو أن رجلاً عمل بِكُلِّ رُخصة : بقول أهل الكوفة في النبيذ، وأهل المدينة في السماع، وأهل مكة فى المتعة، كان فاسقاً." وقال معمر: "لو أن رجلاً أخذ بقول أهل المدينة في السماع يعنى الغناء، وإتيان النساء في أدبارهن، وبقولِ أهل مكة في المتعة والصرف، وبقول أهل الكوفة فى المُسْكر كان أشرّ عباد الله تعالى." وقال سليمانُ السَّيْمِي: "لو أخذت برخصة كل عالم أو قال: زلة كل عالم اجتمع فيك الشر كله." وقال عبدالرحمن بن مهدي رحمه الله تعالى: "لا يكون إماماً في العلم من أخذ بالشاذ، ولا إماماً في العلم من روى عن كل أحد، ولا يكون إماماً من حدث بكل ما سمع." هذا مارأوه في الأقوال الشاذة التي صدرت من الفقهاء الكبار الموثوقين الذين شهد لهم أهل العلم بالتفقه والورع، فما بالك بالأقوال الشاذة الصادرة من بعض من لاعلاقة له بالعلم والفقه وإنّما قال ماقال بناء على آراءه المتطرفة، أو عواطفه النفسية، أو على ثقافات أجنبية لا تمت إلى الإسلام بصلة. فيجب الأخذ بما هو أرجح دليلاً وأقوى حجة بالنظر إلى مصادر الشريعة الإسلامية ومقاصدها النبيلة وأقوال جماهير الفقهاء. الخامس: أن يؤخذ ذلك المذهب بجميع شروطه المعتبرة فيه، لئلا يؤدى ذلك إلى التلفيق فى مسألة واحدة. ومن المناسب أن نذكر هنا بعض التفصيل فى مسألة التلفيق، والله سبحانه ولي التوفيق.
حكم التلفيق
الذي تلخص لي فى موضوع التلفيق أن هذا الاصطلاح يُقصد به في عامة كلام الفقهاء أن يُختار مذهبان فى مسألةٍ واحدةٍ بحيث تحدث منه حالةٌ مركبة لا تجوز في أحد المذهبين مثل أن يأخذ المرأُ بقول الحنفية فى عدم انتقاض الوضوء بمَسَّ المرأة، وبمذهب الشافعية في عدمه بالدم السائل، ويُصلّى بعد ما مست امرأةً وسال منه دم، فإنّ هذه الصلوة لا تصح في أحدٍ من المذهبين. وقال القرافي رحمه الله تعالى: العلامة القرافي: هو أحمد بن أبي العلاء إدريس بن عبد الرحمن القرافي المصري، المالكي، أبو العباس شهاب الدين الإمام الأصولي الذي عدّه الإمام السيوطي من المجتهدين وإن كان منتسبا إلى مذهب الإمام مالك رحمهم الله تعالى، والقرافي نسبة إلى بقعة القرافة بمصر التي سكنها الإمام لمدة يسيرة. ولد رحمه الله سنة ٦٢٦ هـ. وأخذ العلم عن جهابذة علماء عصره كالإمام عزّ الدين بن عبد السلام والإمام ابن الحاجب، صاحب "الكافية" و "الشافية" وغيرهم رحهم الله تعالى. له تصانيف في غاية النفع، منها: "الإحكام في تمييز الفتاوى عن الأحكام"، و "أنوار البروق في أنواء الفروق"، و"الذخيرة" في فروع المالكية وغيرها. تُوفي رحمه الله سنة ٦٨٤ (ملخص من مقدمة التحقيق للفروق لفضيلة الشيخ عمر حسن القيام).
Imam al-Awza'i said: 'Whoever takes from the rare opinions of scholars leaves Islam.' Al-Hafiz al-Dhahabi said: 'Whoever follows the dispensations of the schools and the slips of the mujtahids has weakened his religion, as al-Awza'i and others said: Whoever takes the saying of the Meccans on mut'ah, the Kufans on nabidh, the Medinans on singing, and the Syrians on the infallibility of the caliphs has gathered evil. Similarly, whoever takes in ribawi sales from those who circumvent, and in divorce and analytic marriage from those who are lenient, and similar things, exposes himself to dissolution.' Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal said: 'If a man acted with every dispensation: the saying of the people of Kufa on nabidh, the people of Medina on listening, and the people of Mecca on mut'ah, he would be a sinner.' Ma'mar said: 'If a man took the saying of the people of Medina on listening (meaning singing) and coming to women from behind, and the saying of the people of Mecca on mut'ah and currency exchange, and the saying of the people of Kufa on intoxicants, he would be the worst of Allah's servants.' Sulayman al-Saymi said: 'If you take the dispensation of every scholar—or he said: the slip of every scholar—all evil would gather in you.' Abd al-Rahman ibn Mahdi said: 'He is not an imam in knowledge who takes from the shadhdh, nor an imam in knowledge who narrates from everyone, nor an imam who narrates everything he hears.' This is what they opined regarding the irregular opinions issued by great reliable jurists whom the people of knowledge attested to possess fiqh and piety. What then of the irregular opinions issued by those who have no connection to knowledge and fiqh, but only said what they said based on extremist views, or personal emotions, or foreign cultures that have no relation to Islam? So it is obligatory to take that which is stronger in evidence and more powerful in argument with reference to the sources of Islamic law, its noble objectives, and the statements of the majority of jurists. Fifth: That school is taken with all its valid conditions, so that this does not lead to talfiq in a single issue. It is appropriate to mention here some detail on the issue of talfiq, and Allah is the granter of success.
The Ruling on Talfiq
What has become clear to me on the topic of talfiq is that this term is generally used by jurists to mean that two schools are chosen in a single issue such that a composite situation arises that is not permissible in either of the two schools. For example, a person takes the Hanafi view that wudu is not broken by touching a woman, and the Shafi'i view that it is not broken by flowing blood, and then prays after touching a woman and blood flowed from him. This prayer is not valid in either school. And al-Qarafi said: (footnote: al-Allamah al-Qarafi is Ahmad ibn Abi al-Ala Idris ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Qarafi al-Misri al-Maliki...)
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage is a methodological rule prohibiting the practice of indiscriminately following dispensations and irregularities from different schools, and defines the concept of talfiq (patchwork) in fatwa. The author begins by quoting several early authorities warning that assembling dispensations from various madhhabs leads to moral and religious decay. Al-Awza'i states that taking from rare opinions amounts to leaving Islam. Al-Dhahabi and others warn that following every rukha (concession) and zalla (slip) of scholars weakens one's faith. The passage then cites Imam Ahmad and others to emphasize that such selective picking is tantamount to sinfulness and even the worst of deeds. The key point is that even if the source scholars are reliable, their irregular opinions (shadhdh) should not be followed; how much more so when those opinions come from unqualified persons. The author concludes that one must adopt the view that has the strongest evidence and is most consistent with the goals of sharia and the majority of jurists. Then, as a condition for following another madhhab (the fifth point), the author states that one must follow all the conditions of that madhhab to avoid talfiq in a single issue. He then defines talfiq: combining parts of rulings from different madhhabs in one issue such that the resulting composite act is not valid according to either school. The example given is a person who prays after touching a woman (Hanafi: does not invalidate wudu) and having flowing blood (Shafi'i: does not invalidate wudu); his prayer would be invalid in both madhhabs because the composite situation (touching woman + flowing blood) would break wudu in the Shafi'i school (due to touching) and in the Hanafi school (due to flowing blood, as blood invalidates wudu in Hanafi if it is flowing). The author then begins to cite al-Qarafi, but the passage cuts off. This lesson teaches that talfiq corrupts worship and is prohibited; the mufti and layman must avoid it.

Key Terms
تلفيق (talfīq): Combining rulings from different madhhabs in a single issue such that the composite act is not valid in either school
حالة مركبة (hālah murakkabah): A composite situation resulting from combining rulings from two schools

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the result of talfiq in the example given?
A) The prayer is valid in one school.
B) The prayer is invalid in both schools.
C) The prayer is valid if the person intended to follow both schools.
D) The prayer is valid because each event alone is not a breaker.

Key Takeaway
Talfiq invalidates the act if the composite is not valid in any single school; thus one must follow a complete school in any given issue.
