أصول الإفتاء
٢٣٦
الافتاء بمذهب آخر
ولكن قال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "قلت: وتقييد السلطان له بذلك غير قيد، لما قاله العلامة قاسم فى تصحيحه من أن الحكم والفتوى بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع. وقال العلامة قاسم في فتاواه: وليس للقاضي المقلّد أن يحكم بالضعيف لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح، فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل، ولو حكم لا ينفذ، لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق، لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما وقع من أن القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بين في موضعه.
وهذا يدل أنّ عدم نفاذ القضاء من المقلّد ليس مبه رز حقاً[؟] على كونه مأموراً من السلطان بالقضاء على مذهب معين، بل الحكم كذلك وإن لم يُقيّده السلطان بذلك. وعلة النفاذ أنه عدم بحكم كونه مقلداً مأموران يحكم بصحيح مذهبه. ولكن هذا إذا كان القاضي التزم لنفسه مذهباً معيناً ويراه حقاً، ثمّ قضى بمذهب غيره عامداً خلاف ما يراه حقاً، فإنّ هذا القضاء لا ينفذ، مع كونه في مسئلة مجتهد فيها، وذلك لأنه في حكم المجتهد الذى يقضى بخلاف رأيه، ولا ينفذ مثل هذا القضاء عند أصحابنا الثلاثة، لأنه قضاء بما ليس عنده، فهو متبع فيه هواه. فكذلك المقلد لمذهب معين. أما إذا قضى بمذهب غيره ناسياً مذهبه، نفذ عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، ولم ينفذ عند الصاحبين لأنه خطاً عنده، وذكر صاحب الهداية أنّ الفتوى على قولهما، وفي الفتاوى الصغرى أن الفتوى على قول أبي حنيفة، وذكر ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى أن الوجة فى هذا الزمان أن يُفتى بقول الصاحبين ، لأن التارك لمذهبه لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل ، لالقصدِ جميل
(۱) رد المحتار كتاب الفضاء، فصل فى الحبس ١٦:٤٦٧، فقره ٢٦٣٥٧
(۲) فتح القدير، باب كتاب القاضي إلى القاضي ٦:٣٩٧
Principles of Issuing Fatwa 235: Issuing Fatwa According to Another Madhhab (1) Regarding the enforcement of his judgment, there are two narrations, and the most correct is that it is enforced. As in Khizanat al-Muftin. Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, elaborated in explaining this issue, and mentioned that Allamah Qasim, may Allah have mercy on him, authored a treatise on it, and he summarized it and supported it, stating that his words are of the highest investigation. But the commentary by al-Rafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him, in explaining the issue (2) is more concise and more appropriate, so let it be referred to for verification of this issue, and this is not the place to expand upon it. Judgment of the Muqallid Judge Contrary to the Madhhab of His Imam 6 All the detail that has passed regarding the enforcement of judgment in matters of ijtihad applies in two cases unanimously. The first case: that the judge is a mujtahid, and his judgment coincides with his ijtihad. The second case: that he is a muqallid, and he judged according to the madhhab of his imam; then his judgment is enforced upon everyone, whether the litigants are mujtahids whose opinion contradicts the opinion of the judge's imam, or are muqallids of another imam. As for if the judge is a muqallid of a specific imam, then he judges contrary to his madhhab, they mentioned that it is not enforced. Their expressions differed in its ta'lil (rationale). In Fath al-Qadir, he explained it by saying: 'As for the muqallid, he was appointed only to judge according to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, for example, so he does not have the authority to contradict, so he becomes dismissed with respect to that ruling.' And upon this, the non-enforcement of his judgment is based on the fact that the ruler only made him a judge on the condition that he judge according to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa; if he departs from his madhhab, he becomes dismissed in that judgment, so it is not enforced. The implication of this ta'lil is that if the ruler did not restrict him to a specific madhhab, his judgment in matters of ijtihad is enforced, even if it contradicts the madhhab of his imam. (1) Al-Fatawa al-Hindiyya 3:357, Kitab al-Qada, Bab 9 (2) Refer to Radd al-Muhtar, Kitab al-Qada, Fasl fi al-Habs 16:417, paragraph 263/81, and the words of al-Rafi'i under his statement: 'This is a statement of utmost investigation.' Principles of Issuing Fatwa 236: Issuing Fatwa According to Another Madhhab But Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: 'I say: The ruler's restriction of him to that is not a condition, because of what Allamah Qasim said in his Tashih: that judging and issuing fatwa based on what is marjuh (preponderated against) is contrary to consensus. And Allamah Qasim said in his Fatawa: The muqallid judge is not permitted to judge by the weak (opinion) because he is not qualified for tarjih (preponderance), so he should not deviate from the sahih (sound) except for an ignoble purpose, and if he judges, it is not enforced, because his judgment is a judgment with other than the truth, for the truth is the sahih. And what has occurred that the weak opinion gains strength by judgment, what is meant is the judgment of a mujtahid, as is explained in its place.' And this indicates that the non-enforcement of the judgment from the muqallid is not based on [؟] his being commanded by the ruler to judge according to a specific madhhab, rather the ruling is like that even if the ruler did not restrict him to that. And the cause of non-enforcement is that it is a judgment by virtue of his being a muqallid commanded to judge by the sahih of his madhhab. But this is if the judge has committed himself to a specific madhhab and considers it true, then he judges according to another madhhab intentionally, contrary to what he considers true; then this judgment is not enforced, even if it is in a matter of ijtihad. That is because he is in the position of a mujtahid who judges contrary to his own opinion, and such judgment is not enforced according to our three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), because it is a judgment based on what is not his opinion, so he is following his desire in it. Similarly for the muqallid of a specific madhhab. As for if he judges according to another madhhab while forgetting his own madhhab, it is enforced according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, but not enforced according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because it is an error according to them. The author of al-Hidayah mentioned that the fatwa is according to their statement, while in al-Fatawa al-Sughra the fatwa is according to the statement of Abu Hanifa. Ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that the appropriate course in this time is to issue fatwa according to the statement of the two companions, because the one who abandons his madhhab does so only out of vain desire, not for a noble purpose.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Ifta' deals with the ruling on a muqallid judge who gives a judgment contrary to the madhhab of his imam. It begins with a brief note about a related issue concerning the enforcement of a judgment with two narrations, citing Ibn Abidin and al-Rafi'i. Then it moves to the main section: 'Judgment of the Muqallid Judge Contrary to the Madhhab of His Imam'. The author explains that the general rule for enforcement of judgments in matters of ijtihad applies in two cases: (1) when the judge is a mujtahid and his judgment matches his ijtihad, (2) when the judge is a muqallid and judges according to his imam's madhhab. In both cases, the judgment is enforced. However, if a muqallid judge judges contrary to his imam's madhhab, the scholars have stated that it is not enforced. The author then discusses the ta'lil (rationale) from Fath al-Qadir: the judge is appointed on condition that he judge according to his imam's madhhab; if he violates that condition, he becomes dismissed and his judgment is void. Ibn Abidin critiques this, citing Allamah Qasim, arguing that the condition is not the real issue; rather, the muqallid must judge by the sahih of his madhhab because he is not qualified to choose weak opinions. Thus, even without a ruler's condition, such a judgment is invalid. The passage then differentiates between intentional and forgetful violation: if intentional, it is invalid by all three imams. If forgetful (nasiyan), Abu Hanifa says it is enforced, while the two companions (Sahibayn) say it is not. The author notes that the fatwa in al-Hidayah is with the Sahibayn, but al-Fatawa al-Sughra follows Abu Hanifa, while Ibn al-Humam favors the Sahibayn in this time due to corrupt intentions.

Key Terms
المقلّد (al-muqallid): A judge who follows a specific imam (e.g., Abu Hanifa) and is not qualified for ijtihad or tarjih.
نفاذ القضاء (nufudh al-qada'): The legal enforceability of a judge's verdict; whether it is binding and must be implemented.
المجتهد (al-mujtahid): A judge qualified to derive rulings directly from evidence; his judgment is based on his own ijtihad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the default ruling when a muqallid judge intentionally judges contrary to his own madhhab in a matter of ijtihad?
A) The judgment is enforced if the ruler did not restrict him to a specific madhhab.
B) The judgment is enforced according to Abu Hanifa.
C) The judgment is not enforced according to all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
D) The judgment is enforced only if the muqallid judge forgets his madhhab.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge's judgment contrary to his madhhab is invalid if intentional; if forgetful, the mufta bihi is also invalid due to corrupt times, per Ibn al-Humam.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
advanced
10 min
The Muqallid Judge and Judgment by Another Madhhab
Discussion of enforceability of a muqallid judge's ruling according to another madhhab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which a muqallid judge's ruling according to another madhhab is enforceable and apply the preferred view (mufta bihi) in contemporary fatwa.

Core Idea
A muqallid judge's deliberate deviation from his madhhab voids the ruling; forgetful deviation is disputed but the later view prefers non-enforceability.

This lesson examines a critical rule in the Hanafi tradition regarding a judge who is a muqallid (non-mujtahid) and issues a ruling according to a madhhab other than his own. The passage from Mufti Taqi Usmani's work clarifies that the enforceability depends on the judge's intention and knowledge, and highlights the evolution of the preferred view over time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the judge's status
Determine if the judge is a muqallid or mujtahid, and whether he has adopted a specific madhhab. This is the starting point for applying the rules.
A muqallid is not a mujtahid and must follow his designated madhhab.
2
Distinguish deliberate vs forgetful
Separate the case where the judge intentionally rules against his madhhab from the case where he forgets. The ruling differs significantly.
Deliberate deviation is clearly void; forgetfulness leads to ikhtilaf.
3
Note the ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
Understand that Abu Hanifa enforces the forgetful ruling while Sahibayn do not. This is a valid scholarly difference within the school.
The basis: Abu Hanifa sees valid intention; Sahibayn see error.
4
Apply the later tarjih
Recognize that contemporary practice follows Sahibayn due to concern for vain desire. Ibn al-Humam and later scholars preferred this view.
The mufta bihi in this time is non-enforceability.
5
Consider exceptions
For a judge without a fixed madhhab or a learned muqallid who judges with conditions, different rules apply. These are detailed in the passage.
A judge not committed to any madhhab may rule by taqlid of any reliable jurist.

٢٣٦
الافتاء بمذهب آخر
ولكن قال ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى: "قلت: وتقييد السلطان له بذلك غير قيد، لما قاله العلامة قاسم فى تصحيحه من أن الحكم والفتوى بما هو مرجوح خلاف الإجماع. وقال العلامة قاسم في فتاواه: وليس للقاضي المقلّد أن يحكم بالضعيف لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح، فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل، ولو حكم لا ينفذ، لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق، لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما وقع من أن القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بين في موضعه.
وهذا يدل أنّ عدم نفاذ القضاء من المقلّد ليس مبنيَّاً على كونه مأموراً من السلطان بالقضاء على مذهب معين، بل الحكم كذلك وإن لم يُقيّده السلطان بذلك. وعلة النفاذ أنه عدم بحكم كونه مقلداً مأموراً بأن يحكم بصحيح مذهبه. ولكن هذا إذا كان القاضي التزم لنفسه مذهباً معيناً ويراه حقاً، ثمّ قضى بمذهب غيره عامداً خلاف ما يراه حقاً، فإنّ هذا القضاء لا ينفذ، مع كونه في مسئلة مجتهد فيها، وذلك لأنه في حكم المجتهد الذى يقضى بخلاف رأيه، ولا ينفذ مثل هذا القضاء عند أصحابنا الثلاثة، لأنه قضاء بما ليس عنده، فهو متبع فيه هواه. فكذلك المقلد لمذهب معين. أما إذا قضى بمذهب غيره ناسياً مذهبه، نفذ عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، ولم ينفذ عند الصاحبين لأنه خطأ عنده، وذكر صاحب الهداية أنّ الفتوى على قولهما، وفي الفتاوى الصغرى أن الفتوى على قول أبي حنيفة، وذكر ابن الهمام رحمه الله تعالى أن الوجه فى هذا الزمان أن يُفتى بقول الصاحبين ، لأن التارك لمذهبه لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل، لالقصدِ جميل
أما أذا كان القاضى غير مجتهد، ولم يُقيّده السلطان بمذهب معين ولا التزم هو بمذهب بعينه، فقضى في مسئلة بتقليد أي فقيه معتبر، فالظاهر أنه ينفذ قضاؤه. وذلك لما جاء في الفتاوى الهندية: "ذكر في شرح الطحاوي وجامع الفتاوى القاضى إذالم يكن مجتهداً، ولكنّه قضى بتقليد فقيه، ثم تبين أنه خلاف مذهبه ينفذ وليس لغيره نقضه، وله أن ينقضه. هكذا روى عن محمد رحمه الله تعالى وقال أبويوسف رحمه الله تعالى: ماليس لغيره أن ينقضه، ليس له نقضه. ولأن المتأخرين من الفقهاء الحنفيّة أجازوا تقليد الجاهل القضاء بأن يقضى بفتوى غيره كما في الهداية، ولم يُقيّدوه بأن يلتزم مذهباً معيناً. وكذلك إن كان القاضى المقلد ملتزماً بمذهب معين، ولكنه عالم متبحر، فيتأتى فيه ماذكرنا فى المفتى المقلد الذي يُفتى بمذهب آخر في بعض الحالات بشروط فصلناها في مسئلة الإفتاء بمذهب آخر. ولا يخرجه ذلك عن كونه مقلّدا. فالظاهر أنّه لو قضى فى مسئلةٍ معينة بخلاف قول إمامه وبرأي فقيه آخر يراه حقاً فى تلك المسئلة بالشروط التي قدمناها هناك، ينفذ قضاؤه، ولا يتأتى فيه ماذكره ابن الهمام وغيره من أن التارك لمذهبه لا يفعله إلا لهوى باطل. والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
أمر السلطان أو الأمير فى مسئلةٍ مجتهد فيها
وما ذكرنا من نفاذ قضاء القاضى فى المجتهدات مبني على أنه مولى
Principles of Issuing Fatwa (page numbers). Issuing fatwa according to another madhhab. But Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, said: "I say: The sultan's restriction of him to that is not a valid restriction, because of what Allamah Qasim said in his verification that ruling and issuing fatwa according to a preponderated view is contrary to consensus. And Allamah Qasim said in his fatawa: It is not permissible for a muqallid judge to rule according to a weak view because he is not among the people of tarjih, so he should not deviate from the correct except for an impure motive, and if he rules it is not enforceable, because his judgment is a judgment with falsehood, because the truth is the correct view. And what is reported that the weak view becomes strong by being ruled upon, what is meant is the ruling of a mujtahid, as explained in its place. And this indicates that the non-enforceability of the ruling of a muqallid is not based on his being commanded by the sultan to rule according to a specific madhhab, but the ruling is the same even if the sultan did not restrict him. And the reason for non-enforceability is that he is a muqallid commanded to rule according to the correct view of his madhhab. But that is if the judge has adopted a specific madhhab for himself and considers it true, then he judges according to another madhhab deliberately contrary to what he considers true, then this judgment is not enforceable, even if it is in a matter of ijtihad, and that is because he is like a mujtahid who judges contrary to his own opinion, and such a judgment is not enforceable according to our three imams, because it is a judgment based on what is not his view, so he follows his desire in it. Similarly, the muqallid of a specific madhhab. As for if he judged according to another madhhab forgetting his own madhhab, it is enforceable according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and not enforceable according to the two companions because it is an error according to them. And the author of al-Hidayah mentioned that the fatwa is according to their view, and in al-Fatawa al-Sughra that the fatwa is according to the view of Abu Hanifa. And Ibn al-Humam, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned that the correct view in this time is to issue fatwa according to the view of the two companions, because the one who abandons his madhhab only does so due to vain desire, not for a good purpose. As for if the judge is not a mujtahid, and the sultan did not restrict him to a specific madhhab nor did he adopt a specific madhhab, and he judged in a matter by taqlid of any reliable jurist, then apparently his judgment is enforceable. That is because of what is mentioned in al-Fatawa al-Hindiyyah: "Mentioned in Sharh al-Tahawi and Jami' al-Fatawa: If the judge is not a mujtahid, but he judged by taqlid of a jurist, then it becomes clear that it is contrary to his madhhab, it is enforceable and no one else may overturn it, but he may overturn it. Thus it is narrated from Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him. And Abu Yusuf, may Allah have mercy on him, said: What no one else may overturn, he may not overturn it." And because the later Hanafi jurists permitted the ignorant person's judging by ruling according to the fatwa of others, as in al-Hidayah, and they did not restrict it to his having adopted a specific madhhab. And similarly, if the muqallid judge is committed to a specific madhhab, but he is a learned and deep scholar, then what we mentioned about the muqallid mufti who issues fatwa according to another madhhab in some cases with conditions that we detailed in the issue of issuing fatwa according to another madhhab applies to him. And that does not remove him from being a muqallid. So apparently, if he judged in a particular matter contrary to the view of his imam and according to the opinion of another jurist that he considers true in that matter, with the conditions we presented there, his judgment is enforceable, and what Ibn al-Humam and others mentioned about the one who abandons his madhhab only doing so due to vain desire does not apply to him. And Allah Almighty knows best. The command of the sultan or amir in a matter subject to ijtihad. And what we have mentioned regarding the enforceability of the judge's ruling in matters of ijtihad is based on the fact that he is a [page cut off].
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage addresses the critical rule concerning a muqallid judge who issues a ruling according to a madhhab other than his own. The discussion begins by refuting a potential misunderstanding: the non-enforceability of such a ruling is not merely due to a sultan's restriction, but because the judge, as a muqallid, is obliged to rule by the soundest view of his own madhhab. If he deliberately rules against his own madhhab, the ruling is void, even if the issue is one of ijtihad, as he is following desire. The passage then distinguishes between deliberate and forgetful action: Abu Hanifa holds the forgetful judge's ruling enforceable, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) deem it unenforceable; later authorities prefer the Sahibayn's view in this time to prevent abuse. Next, the case of a judge who has not adopted any specific madhhab is considered: such a judge may rule by taqlid of any reliable jurist, and his ruling is enforceable. Finally, the passage addresses a learned muqallid judge who, in specific matters, judges according to another imam's view that he believes to be correct, subject to conditions. Such a ruling is enforceable, as he is not merely following desire. The passage ends with the beginning of a new section on the sultan's command in ijtihad matters.

Key Terms
مقلد (muqallid): A person who is not a mujtahid and must follow a specific madhhab
إفتاء بمذهب آخر (ifta' bi madhhab akhar): Issuing a fatwa or ruling according to a madhhab other than one's own

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later preferred view (Ibn al-Humam), what is the ruling on a muqallid judge who judges according to another madhhab while forgetting his own?
A) Enforceable according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Not enforceable, because he abandons his madhhab only due to vain desire.
C) Enforceable only if the sultan permits.
D) The judge may choose to enforce or not.

Key Takeaway
A muqallid judge's ruling according to another madhhab is enforceable only if the judge is not committed to a specific madhhab or if he is a learned muqallid meeting strict conditions; otherwise, the ruling is void.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

Fatwa According to Another School by Order of the Sultan
Rasm al-mufti rule on obedience to ruler

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that obedience to the sultan in ijtihadi matters is wajib and issue a fatwa directing compliance even if it contradicts the mufti's own madhhab.

Core Idea
A mufti must direct the public to obey the ruler's decree in ijtihadi matters, even if it contradicts their own madhhab.

This passage from Radd al-Muhtar establishes a key principle in Hanafi usul al-iftā': the sultan's command in matters open to ijtihad creates an obligation to obey. The ruling is supported by a famous precedent involving Abu Yusuf and Muhammad under Caliph Harun al-Rashid. As a mufti, you must understand when and how to issue fatwa in accordance with state authority, balancing madhhab loyalty with public order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principal rule
Read the opening statement: obedience to the sultan is wajib in non-sinful matters. Recognize this as the foundational maxim governing the entire passage.
The key phrase: 'طاعة السلطان واجبة فيما ليس بمعصية'.
2
Analyze the historical precedent
Examine the narration of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad following Ibn Abbas' madhhab on Eid takbirs. Understand that they acted out of obedience to Harun al-Rashid, not because they changed their own school.
Ibn Abidin's gloss clarifies this was 'امتثالاً لا مذهباً'.
3
Derive the legal principle
From the narration, conclude that the sultan's order in ijtihadi matters makes compliance obligatory for the public and the mufti must guide them accordingly.
This is the direct thamarah al-khilaf: the mufti may issue fatwa contrary to his usual madhhab.
4
Extend to subordinate authorities
Note that the same rule applies to amirs appointed by the sultan over a region or army. Their orders are binding on those under their command.
Al-Haskafi's statement from Siyar al-Tatarkhaniyyah, with Ibn Abidin's caution that the order must not be sinful.
5
Apply the rule to a modern scenario
Consider a contemporary Muslim state issuing a law based on a different madhhab. Determine that the mufti should instruct the public to obey, as long as the law does not require sin.
This is a practical skill for issuing fatwa in a pluralistic legal environment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الافتاء بمذهب آخر من قبل السلطان والأصل فيه أن طاعة السلطان واجبة فيما ليس بمعصية، فإن أصدر أمراً فى الأمور المجتهد فيها، وجبت إطاعته. ولذلك روى عن الإمام أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى أنهما كبّرا في صلوة العيد في الأولى سبعاً، وفى الثانية سنّاً على مذهب عبدالله بن عباس رضی الله تعالى عنهما، مع أنّ مذهبهما أنّ التكبيرات الزوائد في العيد سنة على مذهب عبدالله بن مسعود رضى الله تعالى عنه. يقول ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى: "قال في الظهيرية: وهو تأويل ما روى عن أبي يوسف ومحمّد، فإنّهما فَعَلا ذلك لأن هارون أمرهما أن يكبرا بتكبير جده، ففعلا ذلك امتثالاً له، لا مذهباً (1)M واعتقاداً. قال فى المعراج لأنّ طاعة الإمام فيما ليس بمعصية واجبة. والظاهر من هذا أنه لو صدر هناك أمر أو قانون من حاكم مسلم في مسئلة مجتهد فيها، وجب امتثاله على العامة، ولوكان خلاف مذهبهم الفقهي، فيفتى المفتى العامة بامتثاله، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. أمّا الأميرُ الذى ولأه السلطان فى منطقة مخصوصة، أو ولاه قيادة عسكر من عساكر المسلمين، فحكمه كذلك لمن هو تحت إمارته. قال الحصكفي في الدر المختار: "وأمّا الأمير، فمتى صادف فصلاً مجتهداً فيه، نفذ أمره، كما قدمناه عن سير التتارخانية. " وقال ابن عابدین رحمه الله تعالى تحته: "الذى رأيته في سير التتارخانية: قال محمد: وإذا أمر الأمير العسكر بشيء، كان على العسكر أن يطيعوه، إلا أن يكون المأموريه معصية اهـ فقول الشارح: نفذ أمره بمعنى وجب امتثاله تأمل. (۱) رد المحتار، باب العيدين، ٥:١٢١ (۲) (۲) رد المحتار كتاب القضاء، فصل فى الحبس ١٦:٤٦٨ فقره ٢٦٣٥٩
Issuing fatwa according to another school by order of the sultan. The principle is that obedience to the sultan is obligatory in what is not a sin. If he issues an order in matters open to ijtihad, obedience to him is obligatory. For this reason it is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them) that they said the takbir in the Eid prayer seven times in the first rak'ah and five in the second according to the school of Abdullah ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them), even though their own school is that the extra takbirs in Eid are sunnah according to the school of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) says: He said in al-Zahiriyyah: This is an interpretation of what is narrated from Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, for they did that because Harun ordered them to say takbir according to the takbir of his grandfather, so they did that in obedience to him, not as a school of thought or belief. He said in al-Mi'raj: Because obedience to the imam in what is not a sin is obligatory. It appears from this that if there issues an order or law from a Muslim ruler in a matter open to ijtihad, compliance with it is obligatory upon the common people, even if it is contrary to their juristic school. So the mufti gives fatwa to the common people to comply with it. And Allah Most High knows best. As for the amir whom the sultan has appointed over a specific region, or appointed over a military unit of the Muslim army, his ruling is likewise for those under his command. Al-Haskafi said in al-Durr al-Mukhtar: As for the amir, whenever he encounters a ruling open to ijtihad, his command is enforceable, as we have previously mentioned from Siyar al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And Ibn Abidin (may Allah have mercy on him) says below it: What I have seen in Siyar al-Tatarkhaniyyah: Muhammad said: When the amir orders the army with something, it is upon the army to obey him, unless what is commanded is a sin. So the commentator's saying 'his command is enforceable' means compliance is obligatory — consider carefully. (1) Radd al-Muhtar, Book of the Two Eids, 5:121 (2) Radd al-Muhtar, Book of Judgments, Chapter on Imprisonment, 16:468, paragraph 26359.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning fatwa by order of a ruler. The author establishes the principle that obedience to the sultan is obligatory in matters that are not sinful. When the sultan issues an order in a matter subject to ijtihad (i.e., where there are multiple valid opinions), compliance becomes mandatory. This is supported by a historical precedent: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, despite their own school (following Ibn Mas'ud) that the extra takbirs in Eid are five in the first rak'ah and four in the second, performed the prayer with seven and five takbirs following the school of Ibn Abbas, because the Caliph Harun al-Rashid ordered them to do so. Ibn Abidin explains this as an act of obedience, not a change in their personal school. The rule applies to common people (al-'ammah), who must follow the ruler's decree even if it contradicts their usual madhhab. The mufti should instruct them accordingly. The passage further extends this to amirs (princes or military commanders) appointed by the sultan; their orders are binding on those under their authority. However, Ibn Abidin cautions that the amir's command must not be sinful, and he notes a nuance in al-Haskafi's wording—that 'enforceable' (nufidha) means 'obligation to comply' (wajib al-imitithal). This is a critical point for muftis: when state law or a ruler's decree aligns with a different madhhab, they may issue fatwa accordingly, prioritizing social order and obedience over madhhab loyalty.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The political ruler or sovereign authority in the Islamic state.
المجتهد فيها (al-mujtahad fīhā): Matters that are open to ijtihad, i.e., where qualified scholars may differ based on evidence.
امتثال (imtithāl): Compliance or obedience to an order, considered obligatory here.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the reason Abu Yusuf and Muhammad performed Eid prayer with seven takbirs in the first rak'ah, according to Ibn Abidin?
A) They changed their madhhab to that of Ibn Abbas.
B) They were ordered by the caliph Harun al-Rashid, so they obeyed.
C) They found new evidence favoring Ibn Abbas's view.
D) They were uncertain and followed the majority.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must direct the public to obey the ruler's decree in ijtihadi matters, even if it contradicts the mufti's own madhhab, because obedience to the sultan in non-sinful matters is wajib.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa

The Principle of Changing Rulings: Four Mechanisms
Explains the maxim and its four categories of change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim of changing rulings, identify its four mechanisms, and apply the maxim to a real fatwa scenario, while recognizing its limits.

Core Idea
Rulings change through cause, custom, necessity, or blocking means — but not arbitrarily.

This lesson addresses a foundational principle for muftis: rulings may change over time, but only through specific, well-defined mechanisms. Mufti Taqi Uthmani clarifies that the maxim 'Rulings change with changing times' is not universal; change is limited to situations where the cause, custom, necessity, or the need to block means has shifted. Understanding these four mechanisms is essential for issuing sound fatwas in changing contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its qualification
Begin by articulating the maxim as presented in the text: that rulings can change with time, but this does not apply to all rulings. Note the author's warning against the misinterpretation that all rulings are fluid.
The maxim is wusta (intermediate), not kubra (universal).
2
List the four mechanisms
Identify from the passage the four specific ways change can occur: (1) change of the effective cause ('illa), (2) change of custom ('urf), (3) severe necessity (darurah) or general affliction, and (4) blocking means (sadd al-dhara'i').
The author notes that change of custom is actually a subset of change of cause.
3
Understand each mechanism
For each mechanism, explain the trigger and the extent of change. For 'illa: if the cause ceases, the ruling ceases. For custom: if the custom changes, the ruling based on it changes. For necessity: change is limited to the extent of the necessity. For blocking means: permissible means may be restricted to prevent harm.
These mechanisms are not mutually exclusive; sometimes multiple apply.
4
Identify the exception
Recognize that rulings that are purely devotional (ta'abbudi) or based on definitive texts (qat'i) are not subject to change, as their cause or custom is not mutable.
Refer to the istithna' in the qawida panel.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a modern scenario (e.g., use of credit cards, online contracts), determine which mechanism(s) might justify a change in ruling. Provide reasoning step-by-step.
Practice identifying the 'illa or custom involved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان

أصول الإفتاء
٢٤٠
تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان
قد عرف في عبارات الفقهاء أنّ الأحكام تتغيّر بتغيّر الزمان، وليس هذا الأصل كليا بأن يتغير به جميع الأحكام الشرعية، كما زعمه بعض الإباحيين في عصرنا. وإنّما المراد بهذا الأصل أنّ بعض الأحكام تتغير بتغير الزمان وإنما يقع هذا التغير بأحد الوجوه الأربعة الآتية:
الأول: أن يكون الحكم معلولاً بعلّة. فإن فاتت العلة بتغير الزمان، تغيّر الحكم بقواتها.
والثاني: أن يكون الحكم مبنياً على العرف والعادة، فلو تغير العرف تغير الحكم. وهذا في الحقيقة يرجع إلى الوجه الأول، لأن تغير العرف إنما يُغيّر الحكم إن كان الحكم السابق معلولاً بالعُرف.
والثالث: أن يتغيّر الحكم لضرورة شديدة، أو لعموم البلوى. ويقع التغير بقدر الضرورة.
والرابع: أن يتغيّر الحكم لسد الذرائع.
ونريد ههنا أن نشرح هذه الوجوه الأربعة بشيء من التفصيل والله الموفق للصواب.
١- تغير الحكم بتغير العلّة
من المسلّم لدى الفقهاء أن الحكم يدور علي العلة وجوداً و عدماً،
(۱) ذكره الفقهاء في عدة مواضع، فمثلاً ذكره ابن عابدين رحمه الله تعالى في باب الوتر والنوافل، فقال: "فقد تتغير الأحكام لاختلاف الزمان فى كثير من المسائل على حسب المصالح" (رد المحتار: ۳۷۰ فقره (٥٩١٦)
Change of rulings with change of time. It has been known in the statements of the jurists that rulings change with the change of time, and this principle is not universal such that all legal rulings change by it, as some of the permissive ones in our time have claimed. Rather, what is meant by this principle is that some rulings change with change of time, and this change occurs only through one of the following four ways: First: That the ruling is caused by a cause. If the cause ceases due to change of time, the ruling changes due to its cessation. Second: That the ruling is based on custom and habit. If the custom changes, the ruling changes. This in reality reverts to the first way, because change of custom only changes the ruling if the previous ruling was caused by custom. Third: That the ruling changes due to severe necessity or general affliction. The change occurs to the extent of the necessity. Fourth: That the ruling changes to block the means. We intend here to explain these four ways in some detail, and Allah is the granter of success. 1- Change of ruling due to change of cause. It is accepted among the jurists that the ruling revolves around the cause, in existence and non-existence. (1) The jurists mentioned it in several places; for example, Ibn Abidin, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned it in the chapter on Witr and supererogatory prayers, saying: 'For rulings may change due to difference of time in many matters according to interests.' (Radd al-Muhtar: 370, paragraph (5916))
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti (methodological rule for issuing fatwas) from Mufti Taqi Uthmani's work on the principles of ifta. It addresses the maxim 'Rulings change with changing times.' The author immediately qualifies this: the maxim is not universal (kulli) — not every ruling changes. He warns against a misunderstanding by some 'ibahiyyun' (those who take a lax view) who claim all rulings are subject to change. Instead, change occurs only through four specific mechanisms.

First, change due to the cause ('illa): A ruling is tied to its underlying cause. If that cause disappears with time, the ruling changes. This is the foundational mechanism. Second, change due to custom ('urf): Because many rulings are built on prevailing custom, a change in custom can change the ruling. The author notes this is actually a subcategory of the first, because custom functions as the 'illa. Third, change due to severe necessity (darurah) or general affliction ('umum al-balwa): Necessity overrides normal rules, but only to the extent required. Fourth, change due to blocking means (sadd al-dhara'i'): To prevent a forbidden outcome, a permissible means may be restricted; this can also affect rulings over time.

The author then announces his intention to elaborate on each. He begins with the first: 'change due to change of cause,' citing the well-known principle that the ruling follows the cause in existence and non-existence. He supports this with a reference to Ibn Abidin, who stated in Radd al-Muhtar that rulings change due to difference of time according to public interest.

This passage establishes that fatwa authority requires discipline: change is not arbitrary but must be based on clear juristic reasoning from cause, custom, necessity, or blocking means. The reliance on Ibn Abidin indicates the weight of later Hanafi scholarship (mutakhkhirin) in determining when such changes apply.

Key Terms
تغير الأحكام (taghayyur al-ahkam): The modification of a legal ruling due to a change in its cause, custom, necessity, or to block means
علة ('illa): The effective cause (ratio legis) upon which a ruling is based; if it ceases, the ruling ceases
عرف ('urf): Custom or habitual practice that serves as a basis for a ruling; change in 'urf can change the ruling
ضرورة (darurah): Severe necessity that makes lawful what is otherwise prohibited, to the extent needed
سد الذرائع (sadd al-dhara'i'): Blocking the means that lead to forbidden outcomes, even if the means themselves are permissible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the four ways a ruling can change with time?
A) Change in the effective cause ('illa)
B) Change in custom ('urf)
C) Change in the consensus of scholars (ijma')
D) Severe necessity (darurah) or general affliction

Key Takeaway
Rulings change with time only through specific mechanisms: change of cause, custom, necessity, or blocking means; the maxim is not universal.

Explicit and Implicit 'Illa in Jurists' Statements
Explaining the two types of 'illa derived by jurists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between explicit and implicit 'illa in jurists' statements and apply the Hanafi principle for relying on each type in deriving new rulings.

Core Idea
An explicit 'illa (mussarrah) binds the follower; an implicit 'illa (ma'khudha isharatan) is weak and open to dispute.

In this passage, the author explains how jurists deduce causes for rulings that are not directly from Quran and Sunnah. Understanding the difference between explicit and implicit causes is crucial for a mufti when applying rulings to new cases, as it determines the strength of the analogy. The passage provides classic examples from Hanafi fiqh, including handwriting evidence and sajdat al-tilawa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the 'illa
Determine whether the 'illa is explicitly mentioned in the words of the jurists or must be inferred from their statements. This classification determines the strength of the cause.
Explicit causes are found in direct statements like 'the cause is measure and genus'.
2
Classify the 'illa as explicit or implicit
Use the author's two categories: 'illa mussarrah (explicitly stated by jurists) and 'illa ma'khudha isharatan (taken by indication from their words).
The former is binding on followers; the latter is weak.
3
Analyze the handwriting example
The Hanafi ruling that handwriting is not accepted as proof is explicitly justified by the fear of forgery. When this cause is absent (e.g., official registers), the ruling changes.
This illustrates that the ruling revolves with the cause.
4
Analyze the sajdat al-tilawa example
The rulings on parrot and echo indicate that the cause for obligatory prostration is actual human recitation. This cause is not explicitly stated but inferred.
Such implicit causes are considered among the weakest proofs.
5
Assess the reliability of an implicit 'illa
Recognize that implicit causes are open to disagreement and should be applied with caution. The author explicitly states their weakness.
When issuing fatwa, prefer explicit causes whenever possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد تكون العلة غير منصوصة فى القرآن والسنّة، ولكن يستنبطها الفقهاء بالدلائل الشرعيّة. وهي علي قسمين أيضا.
فالقسم الأوّل: ما ذكره الفقهاء بألفاظ صريحة، كقول الحنفية إن العلة في تحريم ربا الفضل هي القدرُ والجنس أوقول الشافعية إنّ العلة الطعم والثّمنيّة. فيجب لأصحاب هؤلاء الفقهاء أن يتمسكوا بهذه العلة المصرحة في عبارات فقهاءهم.
ومن هذا القسم ماذكره فقهاء الحنفية من عدم الحكم بالخط كما جاء في المتون، فمثلاً جاء فى تنوير الأبصار وغيره أن المحاضر والسجلات ليست حجة، فلابد من الشهادة على مضمون المكتوب (۱) حتى أنه لا يُقبل خطوط العدول والقُضاة الماضين لإثبات وقف (۳) ولكن عللوه بأن الخط يُشبه الخط، فلا يؤمن من التزوير. وهذه العِلّة مصرحة في كلامهم، فحيث انتفت العلة ووقع الأمن من التزوير جاز العمل بالخط. ولذلك استثنوا من هذا الحكم أشياء، فقالوا يُعْمَل بخط السمسار والبياع والصراف، ويُحْكم عليهم بخطهم. وكذلك ذكر المتأخرون أن بعض الوثائق الحكومية، مثل الدفاتر السلطانية، حجّةٌ يُحكم بها، إذ لا تُحرّر إلا بإذن السلطان، ثم بعد اتفاق الجم الغفير على نقل ما فيها من غير تساهل بزيادة أو نقصان، تُعرض على المُعين لذلك، فيضع خطه عليها، ثمّ تُعرض على المتولى لحفظها، فيكتب عليها، ثمّ تُعاد أصولها إلى أمكنتها المحفوظة بالختم، فالأمن من التزوير مقطوع به. (۱)
والقسم الثاني: علة لم يصرح بها الفقهاء، ولكنّها تؤخذ إشارةً من كلامهم وذلك مثل ما ذكره الفقهاء من أن سجدة التلاوة لا تجب على من سمعها من الببغاء، أو على من سمعها من الصدى. (۳) ويؤخذ من كلامهم إشارة أن علة وجوب السجدة: هي تلاوة إنسان بالفعل، وبما أن صوت الببغاء ليس تلاوةً من إنسان لم تجب به السجدة، وبما أن صوت الصدى ليس تلاوة بالفعل، لم تجب فيه السّجدة. فمن هنا يُستنبط أن سجدة التلاوة غير واجبة إذا سمع الرجل الآية من المُسجل، لأنها ليست تلاوة إنسان بالفعل. ولكن مثل هذه العلة من أضعف العلل ثبوتاً، وفيه مجال للخلاف.
And the cause may not be explicitly mentioned in the Quran and Sunnah, but the jurists deduce it through legal proofs. And it is also of two types. The first type: what the jurists have mentioned in explicit terms, such as the Hanafis saying that the cause for prohibition of riba al-fadl is measure (qadr) and genus (jins), or the Shafi'is saying that the cause is edibility (tu'm) and price (thamaniyya). Thus it is necessary for the followers of these jurists to adhere to this cause that is explicitly stated in the expressions of their jurists. And of this type is what the Hanafi jurists mentioned regarding not judging by handwriting as found in the matn texts. For example, it is stated in Tanwir al-Absar and elsewhere that court records and registers are not valid evidence, so testimony on the content of the writ is necessary (1) to the extent that the handwriting of upright persons and past judges is not accepted to prove a waqf (3). But they explained it by saying that handwriting resembles handwriting, so forgery cannot be ruled out. This cause is explicit in their words. So whenever the cause is absent and safety from forgery is assured, acting on handwriting is permitted. For this reason they made exceptions to this ruling and said that one acts on the handwriting of a broker, seller, and moneychanger, and judgment is passed based on their handwriting. Likewise, later scholars mentioned that some government documents, such as official registers, are valid evidence and judgment is passed thereby, since they are not written except by the permission of the sultan, and after the agreement of a large group on transmitting what is in them without leniency in addition or subtraction, they are presented to the person appointed for that, who places his signature on them, then presented to the custodian for preservation, who writes on them, then the originals are returned to their places preserved with seals, so safety from forgery is certain (1). The second type: a cause that the jurists have not explicitly stated, but it is taken by indication from their words. For example, what the jurists mentioned that the prostration of recitation is not obligatory upon one who hears it from a parrot or from an echo (3). From their words it is taken by indication that the cause for the obligation of prostration is the actual recitation of a human being. Since the sound of a parrot is not a recitation by a human being, the prostration is not obligatory, and since the sound of an echo is not actual recitation, the prostration is not obligatory. From this it is derived that the prostration of recitation is not obligatory if a man hears the verse from a recording, because it is not the actual recitation of a human being. But such a cause is among the weakest causes in terms of proof, and there is room for disagreement.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage discusses the types of 'illa (legal cause) that are not explicitly mentioned in the primary sources but are deduced by jurists. The author divides these into two categories: explicit (mussarrah) in the words of the jurists, and implicit (ma'khudha isharatan) from their statements. In the first category, the jurists have clearly stated the 'illa for a ruling, such as the Hanafi position that the cause for riba al-fadl is measure and genus, or the Shafi'i position that it is edibility and price. In such cases, followers must adhere to these explicit causes. The author provides an example from Hanafi law: handwriting (khatt) is not accepted as proof because of the risk of forgery, as explicitly stated by Hanafi jurists. However, if the cause (fear of forgery) is absent, then acting on handwriting becomes permissible, and exceptions such as the handwriting of a broker or official registers are allowed. The second category involves causes that are not explicitly stated but are inferred from the jurists' statements. The example given is the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa): from the rulings that hearing the prostration from a parrot or echo does not obligate prostration, we infer that the 'illa is actual recitation by a human. This allows us to derive the ruling for recordings. However, such implicit causes are weak and subject to disagreement.

Key Terms
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or ratio legis for a legal ruling, derived by jurists from textual or contextual indications.
علة مصرحة ('illa mussarrah): A cause explicitly stated in the words of the jurists (not necessarily in Quran/Sunnah).
علة مأخوذة إشارة ('illa ma'khudha isharatan): A cause inferred indirectly from the jurists' statements without being explicitly mentioned.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the 'illa for the obligation of sajdat al-tilawa?
A) Hearing any sound resembling Quran recitation
B) Actual recitation of a human being
C) The presence of the Quranic verse
D) The intention of the reciter

Key Takeaway
The strength of a derived 'illa depends on whether it is explicitly stated by jurists (strong) or only inferred (weak and contestable).

Deriving Implicit 'Illah from Juristic Patterns
Explaining how to extract an unstated ratio legis from fuqaha's rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive an implicit 'illah from the patterns of Hanafi fiqh rulings and apply it to a new case, evaluating the strength of the derivation.

Core Idea
An ‘illah inferred from juristic examples is weaker than an explicit one—handle with caution.

In this lesson, we explore a subtle method of legal reasoning: extracting an unstated ratio legis ('illah) from the collective rulings of the Hanafi fuqaha. Rather than declaring the cause directly, the early masters gave rulings that imply a common thread. Your task is to identify that thread, formulate the 'illah, and appreciate its evidentiary weight—or lack thereof—when issuing fatwas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Examples
The passage cites two rulings: (1) sajdat al-tilawah is not obligatory when hearing the verse from a parrot, and (2) not obligatory when hearing from an echo. Note the common element: in both cases, the sound is not a direct human recitation.
These examples are taken from the fatwa literature, likely from Fatawa Hindiyya.
2
Extract the Common Feature
Determine what is absent in both examples that would otherwise trigger the obligation. The passage states that the obligation arises from 'actual human recitation' (tilawah insan bil-fi'l). Both examples lack this: the parrot mimics, the echo reflects.
Think of this as a negative inference: the ruling changes when a specific condition is missing.
3
Formulate the Implicit 'Illah
From the pattern, we infer that the 'illah for wajib sajdat al-tilawah is 'actual human recitation occurring at the time of hearing'. This is not stated explicitly but is deduced from the exceptions.
In usul terms, this is istinbat al-'illah bi al-isharah (deriving the cause by indication).
4
Apply the 'Illah to a New Case
The passage extends the ruling to hearing from a recorder (musajjil). Since a recording is not live human recitation, the same 'illah applies, and the prostration is not obligatory. This is a qiyas on the original examples.
The recorder case is a modern development not explicitly covered by the early fuqaha, but the inferred 'illah allows extension.
5
Evaluate the Strength of the Derivation
The author classifies such an 'illah as among the weakest (min ad'af al-'ilal thubutan). It is open to disagreement because the inference is not explicit; other scholars might identify a different 'illah. As a mufti, you must present such rulings with appropriate qualification.
This step is crucial for adab al-mufti: acknowledge the potential for ikhtilaf and avoid presenting the ruling as definitive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقسم الثاني: علة لم يصرح بها الفقهاء، ولكنّها تؤخذ إشارةً من كلامهم وذلك مثل ما ذكره الفقهاء من أن سجدة التلاوة لا تجب على من سمعها من الببغاء، أو على من سمعها من الصدى. (۳) ويؤخذ من كلامهم إشارة أن علة وجوب السجدة: هي تلاوة إنسان بالفعل، وبما أن صوت الببغاء ليس تلاوةً من إنسان لم تجب به السجدة، وبما أن صوت الصدى ليس تلاوة بالفعل، لم تجب فيه السّجدة. فمن هنا يُستنبط أن سجدة التلاوة غير واجبة إذا سمع الرجل الآية من المُسجل، لأنها ليست تلاوة إنسان بالفعل. ولكن مثل هذه العلة من أضعف العلل ثبوتاً، وفيه مجال للخلاف.
And the second type: an 'illah (ratio legis) not explicitly stated by the fuqaha, but it is taken as an indication from their words. That is like what the fuqaha mentioned: that the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) is not obligatory upon one who hears it from a parrot, or upon one who hears it from an echo. And from their words, an indication is taken that the 'illah for the obligation of the prostration is: the actual recitation of a human. And since the sound of a parrot is not the recitation of a human, the prostration is not obligatory by it; and since the sound of an echo is not actual recitation, the prostration is not obligatory in it. From here, it is derived that the prostration of recitation is not obligatory if a man hears the verse from a recorder, because it is not the actual recitation of a human. But such an 'illah is among the weakest 'illahs in certainty, and there is room for disagreement in it.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage presents the second type of 'illah (ratio legis) in usul al-ifta: an 'illah that is not explicitly stated by the early jurists but is inferred from the patterns in their rulings. The example given is the ruling on sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The fuqaha ruled that prostration is not obligatory if one hears the verse from a parrot or from an echo. By examining these exceptions, we deduce that the 'illah for obligation is actual human recitation (tilawah insan bil-fi'l). Since a parrot's sound is not human recitation, and an echo is not a real recitation (it is a reflection), the prostration is not required. By analogy (qiyas), hearing a verse from a recording also lacks actual human recitation at the moment of hearing, so the ruling extends to that case. However, the author notes that this type of inferred 'illah is weak in terms of certainty (thubut) and is open to differing scholarly views. A mufti must handle such derivations with caution, acknowledging the potential for ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
علة ('illah): The ratio legis or effective cause that grounds a legal ruling; here it is not explicitly stated but inferred from the patterns of rulings.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): A prostration performed upon reciting or hearing certain verses of the Quran; its obligation is conditioned on actual human recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because a recorder is not a human being.
B) Because the sound from a recorder is not actual human recitation (tilawah insan bil-fi'l).
C) Because the recorder's sound is like an echo.

Key Takeaway
An implicit 'illah inferred from juristic patterns is a valid but weak basis for extending rulings; a mufti must present such fatwas with appropriate caution.
